International Commercial Telegrams - Special Commercial Telegrams from Reuters on August 20 65

Gold and Silver

British Gold: The London gold price today was 240 shillings and one penny, a further drop of one and a half pennies.

Central Bank: The London silver market was quite quiet. The spot price remained unchanged at 19 pence. Futures fell by 0.375 to 28.1475. China and India sold, and the United States bought. The currency market stabilized, and futures were sluggish due to Indian sales.

Exchange Rates

British-American: The London foreign exchange market had good trading this morning, with no major price changes. The pound was slightly lower. The opening exchange rate between the British pound and the US dollar was 4.9825. Yesterday's US-British market closed 0.25 higher. Within the first hour, it rose by 0.06. There have been no changes since then.

British-French: The opening price was 0.02 francs, up a fraction. It rose in the middle of the day, and continued to rise in the afternoon. The rate was 70 francs.

Cotton and Wheat

US Cotton: The New York cotton market opened lower because there has been no concrete announcement regarding cotton loans. The market continued to decline afterward, but the market stabilized shortly after. Today's general opinion is that the market is being manipulated by speculation. The rumor that Secretary of Agriculture Wallace Yang will resign if the government approves the loan of 0.02 per pound of cotton is not valid.

British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was slightly soft today. In the afternoon, the October futures price fell two points to 6.01.

British Wheat: The Liverpool market was stable this morning. At 1:00 PM, the October futures price was 6 shillings, 4 pence and 7375, the same as yesterday's closing price. US Wheat: The New York wheat market opened unchanged, but prices rose rapidly due to continued progress in domestic and overseas conditions. Coarse grains opened with a slight decline, but despite continued favorable weather conditions, prices rose in sympathy with the wheat market.

Rubber

London: The London rubber market remained quiet this morning. The成交 prices for October and December futures were 5.75 pence at noon, the same as yesterday's price.

New York: The New York rubber market opened lower due to increased inventories in London and the United States. The market stabilized after the decline.

Securities

New York: New York securities opened slightly lower again today due to continued profit-taking by bulls. It is expected that the amendment to the Wheeler Public Utility Act will be passed by Congress before it adjourns, so public utility stocks weakened again. Although domestic and foreign political situations are unsettled, market sentiment is still strong. Shortly after the opening, market prices trended upward, with some divergence. Railroad stocks and oil stocks were quite stable, steel stocks showed improvement, and other metal stocks also rose in price due to reports that a certain strong European country had ordered hardware. Impressions of a Trip to the South 66

— Special Correspondent Qian Hua of This Newspaper

(Seventeen) Nanning, the Political Center

The Guangxi Provincial Government's reception of members of various academic societies was well-organized. Before most of them left Wuzhou for Nanning, they distributed a book entitled "Notes on Traveling in Guangxi," which had been printed in a rush. The book detailed the history, transportation, and scenic spots of various places. Each member held a copy, which made sightseeing and visiting more convenient after arriving in Nanning. Nanning is the provincial capital with numerous government agencies, making it the political center of the province. The county has an area of 16,904 square li and a population of 352,116. The newly built combined office building of the provincial government is magnificent and modern. The annual conference venue was set up in the provincial government auditorium. The city's roads are flat, and the bustling streets are full of merchants. All the equipment of modern cities is available, such as automatic telephones, running water, and wireless radio stations. However, it is just a miniature version. In recent days, the reporter has visited the museum, printing factory, water plant, radio station, library, livestock conservation, medical school, livestock conservation institute, native cloth factory, dyeing and weaving factory, National Basic Education Research Institute, and leather factory. Most of these are in their initial stages. Although the equipment is relatively simple, their hard work and dedication to serving the people can be seen everywhere. Highways reach all counties, and transportation depends on public buses and automobiles. Rickshaws are extremely rare, not to mention sedan chairs. Nine out of ten people can walk comfortably. Laborers enter the city from the suburbs in the morning and return to their hometowns in the evening, traveling dozens of li every day. They are used to it. Diligence, thrift, and endurance are their characteristics. Therefore, a small number of public buses are sufficient. Most of the private cars are the latest streamlined models. In addition to a few high-ranking officials who have their own cars, there are also car rental companies. The Fourth Group Army Headquarters and the provincial government, the two major institutions, have many official cars for senior officials to ride in, so street traffic is easy to maintain. Those who travel to Guilin always say that the authorities advocate humanitarianism and prohibit rickshaws from running on the streets. According to people in the provincial government, this is not true. Humanitarianism should be advocated, but it is definitely not prohibited by order. In Wuzhou, you can see rickshaws. Nanning has also had several people start rickshaw companies, but they have failed after a short trial. This is because of a natural trend. People are accustomed to hard work and do not need to spend money to have others take their place, which is also a fact.

(Eighteen) Liu Yongfu's Military Flag

Although the Nanning Museum is not large and does not have many exhibits, its arrangement is well-organized, and the selection of materials and simple explanations can arouse public interest and are beneficial to social education. When the reporter visited, women and children were particularly crowded, pointing and explaining as if they had learned something. The most valuable exhibits include the costumes, daily necessities, musical instruments such as bells and drums, talismans, and various superstitious images of the Miao and Yao ethnic groups in Guizhou Province in the first room. There are also handwritten vulgar works such as love letters and love songs of young men and women of the Miao and Yao ethnic groups, which are all treasures. Secondly, there is the Guangxi Special Products Exhibition, the distribution of Guangxi's minerals and crops, and portraits of famous people from Guangxi in history hanging on the walls. The ancient objects such as bells and tripods unearthed in various parts of Guangxi also make considerable contributions to geography, history, archeology, and ethnology. In the eighth room, the trophies of the Fourth Group Army during the Northern Expedition are displayed. On the left wall hangs a square military flag of Liu Yongfu's army, about seven or eight feet long, made of black cloth with white characters. Small characters say "Guangdong and Guangxi Governor's Standard, Rear Battalion of the Fu Army." In the center is a large character "Liu." According to people in the museum, this flag was just donated by Liu Yunxi, the principal of Bobai Middle School, last week and displayed here. Liu's grandfather, Liu Mingguang, once served as the battalion commander of the Fu Army. In 1883, he participated in the Sino-French War. "In 1885, after the Sino-French peace talks, Liu Yongfu and Liu Mingguang returned to their ancestral home in Bobai. This flag was kept in Liu's family. There are still Fu Army seals and other items that are also planned to be donated to the museum for display in the near future. Liu's achievements in resisting foreign enemies are recorded in history. Today, looking at the relics, I can't help but feel awe.

(Nineteen) The Facilities of Hygiene Administration

When the reporter visited the Provincial Medical College, he met with Dean Ge Shaolong. Ge is the cousin of Ge Gongzhen. They talked very happily. According to Ge, the medical college started operating in November of last year. The provincial government gives an annual budget of 110,000 yuan. It also has outpatient clinics in various departments, with 26 internal and surgical doctors and professors, more than 40 undergraduate students, and more than 50 nurses. Its purpose is to train hygiene cadres. All students are tuition-free and are sent to serve in various rural areas after graduation. Guizhou Province pays close attention to the facilities of hygiene administration. Guizhou is vast and sparsely populated. Sound hygiene administration, in the active aspect, rapidly increases the production rate under healthy conditions, and in the preventive aspect, can gradually reduce the devastation of epidemics. The Guizhou Provincial Government has established a Hygiene Committee, whose standing members are the Director of the Education Department, the Director of the Civil Affairs Department, the Director of the Military Medical Department of the General Headquarters, and myself. The committee plans the province's hygiene administration affairs. In various countries, hygiene expenses account for 17 percent of the country's administrative expenses in the United States, 13 percent in Japan, and about one-thousandth in our country. In Guizhou Province, it accounts for a little more than 7 percent of the province's administrative expenses. The budget for hygiene expenses in the 24th year of the Republic was more than 900,000 yuan. The province's more than 90 counties are divided into eight districts. Each district has a provincial hospital, which also manages various hygiene administration affairs. Those that have been established include Wuzhou, Guilin, and Nanning. Wuzhou also has a pharmaceutical factory that produces various anti-epidemic vaccines. Liuzhou has already sent people to prepare. Longzhou, Baise, and Pingle have also prepared to send people to these cities in succession. In addition, it is planned to set up a hygiene experiment institute and a drug planting experiment field in Nanning or Wuzhou. In terms of epidemic prevention, it is one of the most important tasks of hygiene administration. Staff members are sent to various rural villages from time to time to inject anti-epidemic vaccines. In the past, people often said that the southwestern border had a lot of miasma, and those who were affected would become ill or even die. Longzhou and Baise on the border of Guizhou Province were even worse. The mortality rate was shocking. The sparse population is also the biggest reason for this. What exactly is miasma? Doctors have carefully studied it many times. Our college also pays special attention to this disease, sending staff to Longzhou, Baise and other places to investigate and treat it. Three weeks ago, it was reported that more than 300 people died of miasma in a village in Baise. It has recently been found that what is called miasma is actually a tropical disease, malaria. The fever lasts for a long time, or it may not subside completely. In severe cases, people can die in three or four hours. It spreads very quickly and is very scary. Taking a small amount of quinine every day can prevent the epidemic. In addition, leprosy is most prevalent in Guangdong and Guizhou. It is currently planned to set up a large-scale leprosy hospital in Longzhou. It is hoped that philanthropists from all over the world will enthusiastically support it and provide economic assistance.

Instability in the Bombay Silver Market 67

(London) Rumors of difficulties in the Bombay silver market were caused by large-scale sales by India in London today. The US government is currently maintaining the spot price to stabilize it, but the futures price has plummeted. The London silver market was slightly unstable today, fearing that the financial difficulties of a certain merchant in Bombay would affect other merchants, which would cause the Bombay silver price to fall and India to sell even more in the London market. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

Bombay: The Bombay silver market opened very late today, and sentiment was unstable. Trading was limited due to rumors that some important merchants would not be able to fulfill their obligations at the current settlement. It is reported that the board of directors of the exchange will meet tonight. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

Bombay: The import of gold and silver into Bombay during the week ending August 17 was less than in the previous week. The total import value of gold this week was 66,381 rupees, while the value last week was 208,257 rupees. The value at the same time last year was 121,101 rupees. The total import value of silver this week was 287,428 rupees, while the value last week was 284.479 rupees. The value at the same time last year was 202.380 rupees. (Reuters dispatch on the 19th)

Statistics on Flooding in Western Shandong - Survey Before August 10 - Floodwaters Have Risen Sharply and the Disaster Situation is Even More Severe 68

Jinan Communication: There are 10 counties in western Shandong - Jining, Jiaxiang, Juye, Yuncheng, Juancheng, Heze, Dongping, Wenshang, Jinxiang, and Yutai. The total area is 12,465,967 mu (purely cultivated land). The total population of each county is 3,600,1105 people. This time, (the cultivated land) the number of flooded villages is 6,341 villages, the total number of victims is 2,292,589 people, and the amount of property loss is 98,145,136 yuan. Among them, the disaster situation in Juancheng, Juye, Jiaxiang, Dongping, and Yutai counties is the most serious. The disaster statistics of each county are recorded as follows:

Jining

The total area of the county is 2,056,216 mu. The total population of the county is 578,200 people. 100 li of the Grand Canal embankment was affected, the flooded area is about 1,400,000 mu, more than 500 villages were affected, and the affected population is about 400,000 people. The property loss is about 5 million yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 300 villages including Wang Guitun in the southwest. Relief centers, temporary hospitals, and victim transportation stations have now been established to provide relief and transport more than 20,000 victims to various counties (specifically referring to those from this county).

Jiaxiang

The total area of the county is 500,431 mu. The total population of the county is 145,185 people. There is no river embankment. The flooded area is 467,931 mu, 324 villages, and 133,783 victims. The property loss is 3,260,651 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 200 villages between the Zhao Wang River and the Shu River.

Juye

The total area of the county is 2,400,9061 mu. The total population of the county is 354,993 people. There is no river embankment. The flooded area is 1,369,140 mu, more than 1,700 villages, and more than 330,000 victims. The property loss is 22,850,000 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 600 villages from Kangji to the county seat in the northern part of the county.

Yuncheng

The total area of the county is 1,800,9910 mu. The total population of the county is 489,654 people. 60 li of the Yellow River embankment was affected. The flooded area is more than 1,058,000 mu, 686 villages, and more than 330,000 victims. The property loss is more than 220,000 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 300 villages near Wang Laohu Village in the south.

Juancheng

The total area of the county is 835,422 mu. The total population of the county is 283,855 people. 70 li of the Yellow River embankment and 70 li of the Yellow River levee were affected. The flooded area is 600,000 mu, more than 700 villages, and more than 190,000 victims. The property loss is 18,400,000 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 400 villages including Linpuji south of the dam (because the county is close to the mouth of the river, the escape was not timely, and all property was lost to the east, so the loss was particularly heavy, and eight or nine tenths of the land was mud and sand, so the loss was even greater, but it is not included in this statistic).

Heze

The total area of the county is 1,400,1214 mu. The total population of the county is 10. The flooded area is 741,106 mu, 394 villages, and 220,783 victims. The property loss is 3,100,4893 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 200 villages including Yan Shikuo north of the Qili River.

Dongping

The total area of the county is 1,243,520 mu. The total population of the county is 413,725 people. 20 li of the Yellow River embankment and 50 li of the large and small Qing River embankments were affected. The flooded area is 773,854 mu, 530 villages, and 286,743 victims. The property loss is 11,853,592 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 300 villages in the Anshan area in the southwest.

Wenshang

The total area of the county is 1,400,000 mu. The total population of the county is 421,044 people. 90 li of the Wen River embankment was affected. The flooded area is 784,000 mu, more than 300 villages, and 145,700 victims. The property loss is 3,288,000 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 100 villages including Menguanji.

Jinxiang

The total area of the county is 936,851 mu. The total population of the county is 263,812 people. The affected area of the river embankment is more than 200,000 mu, 107 villages, and more than 67,000 victims. The property loss is more than 1.2 million yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 50 villages including Mian Gu Dui in the northeast.

Yutai

The total area of the county is 869,242 mu. The total population of the county is 215,874 people. 120 li of the Nanyang Lake embankment was affected. The flooded area is 740,000 mu, more than 1,100 villages, and 188,580 victims. The property loss is 7,288,000 yuan. The most severely affected areas are the more than 500 villages including Makeng.

(Remarks) (1) The rainfall this year was dry in the spring and early summer in each county. Since entering the Dog Days, there have been continuous heavy rains. (2) The relief situation in each county is that relief centers have been set up, and victims have been transported to Jining and then distributed to various counties for resettlement, or sent directly to Tai'an, Jinan, etc. (3) At present, there are still victims in each county in the water, on rooftops, and on mountaintops, estimated to be no less than 50,000 people per county. Not only do they have no clothes or food, but it is also impossible to find a square of dry land to stand on (4) The above survey was conducted before August 10. Now the floodwaters have risen sharply, and the disaster situation is even more tragic than before.

Suzhou - Two Kidnapped Victims Escape from the Bandit's Den 69

Zhou Pinshan, a farmer from Wangjia Village, Wangting Township, is quite well-off. Last month, Zhou and his 12-year-old eldest son, Longsheng, were kidnapped by bandits, who demanded a ransom of 5,000 yuan. Because the family could not raise the cash, they have not been redeemed yet. Unexpectedly, the bandits took Zhou Pinshan and his son to a boat in Taihu Lake and hid them. On the 19th, they were transported to the reeds on the lakeside for the night. When the bandits watching the victims were sound asleep deep in the night, Zhou Pinshan and his son took the opportunity to swim to the shore. They escaped home yesterday, and the family was overjoyed.

Wuxi - Strict Handling of Private Seed Traffickers in the County District 70

The Wuxi Sericulture Model District, in view of the shortage of silkworm seeds in the spring of this year, which caused a great turmoil, has made early preparations for this autumn seed. The district has ordered various seedbeds to produce as many seeds as possible, which are actually sufficient for distribution. The district has also distributed the seeds to various guidance stations in advance on the 15th, and then distributed them to the silkworm farmers in batches from the 17th to the 20th, in order to prevent seed traffickers from manipulating the market and hoarding. Unexpectedly, various traffickers still used the excuse of free trade and claimed that there was still a large shortage of seeds, and manipulated the market in secret. The Construction Department and the Sericulture Model District have received telegrams from the County Party Headquarters Supervision Committee and local people, one after another, requesting an investigation and ban on seed traffickers raising prices and hoarding. The district immediately telegraphed the county magistrate to order the County Public Security Bureau, together with the model district, to send personnel in disguise for secret investigation. The previous night, Ge Xinde, a supervisor of the Public Security Bureau, first used banknotes with a seal, and bought ten Tiger Brand seeds at the Datong Inn on the road, at a price of 6 jiao per seed, which was an increase of 2 jiao from the original quota. The evidence was conclusive. He immediately led the police to investigate and found 100 Heping Brand seeds without a certificate of qualification. The inn's accountant, Wang Senlin, and the innkeeper's wife, Zhang (nicknamed Black Fish Head), were all taken to the bureau. Yesterday morning (20th), Zhang Zhaozhen, the manager of Datong, voluntarily turned himself in to the bureau and explained everything. After Director Chen interrogated him, he was sent to the county government for interrogation together.

Investigation of Assassination by Opening the Coffin 71

Fan A-quan, a resident of Beixingtang Village, District 7, was murdered on a ferryboat on the night of the 5th of this month. The deceased's uncle, Fan Yongshen, the village head Fan Bingda, and Fan Yunting, Madam Chen Zhu, etc., reported to the court requesting that the coffin be opened for inspection. Upon receiving the report, the Procuratorate dispatched bailiff Huang Yong to the village to seal the coffin and escort it to the river at the Diaqiao Bridge outside Ximen. Village head Jiang Zixian of Huishan also constructed a shed at the desolate tomb behind Wanshou Temple, setting up the scene. Yesterday (the 20th), at 7:40 AM, Prosecutor Shen Zhaoming led coroner Wang, bailiffs, and others to conduct the inspection. Upon arriving at the scene, they ordered workers to open the coffin. Coroner Wang then removed the deceased's skull, which was already black and severely decomposed, making examination difficult. The rotten flesh was scraped off, placed in a wooden basin, and washed with clean water. Then, three sections of the cervical vertebrae were removed and washed in the same manner. Coroner Wang completed the washing and examination at 8:45 AM, covering the skull and three sections of the cervical vertebrae with scallion roots and coarse paper, pouring sorghum liquor over them, and removing them after ten minutes. After examination according to the law, it was found that there was a bluish color on the temporal bone, and red color was discovered on the cervical vertebrae. Two upper incisors, one upper canine tooth, two lower incisors, and two lower canine teeth also had red color, indicating that the deceased was strangled to death before. After the examination, the corpse's relative, Fan Yongshen, was ordered to inspect the body. Fan stated that the left and right cheeks and cheekbones also had red color, which he presumed was caused by blows. Coroner Wang stated that this type of red color was insignificant and would not be fatal even if struck. At this point, Prosecutor Shen ordered workers to place the skeletal remains in the coffin, seal it, and put it under guard for burial in the countryside. The three sections of the cervical vertebrae and seven upper and lower incisors were taken to the court for preservation. The suspects Fan Wenqing, Fan Shigen, and the deceased's concubine, Xi Xiaomei, were also taken to the court. Prosecutor Shen then opened the court for interrogation. As a result, Xi Xiaomei, Fan Shigen, and Fan Wenqing were each ordered to be detained, and the plaintiff, Fan Yongshen, was ordered to return home to await further investigation.

Drug Dealer Li Zengxiang Executed with Sorrow 72

Drug dealer Li Zengxiang (age 51), along with Yang Shuming and He De, were found guilty after interrogation by the Zhenjiang Garrison Command. They were sentenced accordingly. Li Zengxiang was found guilty of violating Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations on the Strict Prohibition of Potent Narcotics for selling red pills and sentenced to death. Yang Shuming was sentenced to sixteen years in prison for assisting in selling red pills. He De was given a reduced sentence of six years in prison because he was helping to keep the red pills. The case was returned to the local county government for execution. Yesterday (the 20th) at 4:00 PM, the county magistrate had Li Zengxiang brought from the detention center, verified his identity, tied him up, and executed him by firing squad at the South School Field.

Zhenjiang: Implementation of Reward and Punishment Measures for Promoting Compulsory Education 74

In order to reward and punish the promotion of compulsory education, the Jiangsu Provincial Government issued a general order to all counties yesterday, stipulating that counties that should increase fifty school levels and can establish them on schedule and in full number will have their county magistrates credited to commend their achievements. If less than half are established at one time, they should be penalized for their negligence. Counties that should increase ten to fifteen school levels will be commended if they can establish fifteen school levels. Those who fail to establish ten levels will be penalized. Educational administrative personnel will be assessed by the Department of Education and rewarded or punished accordingly. Most of the funding for new compulsory schools has been subsidized by the central government and provincial funds. Counties must ensure that the small amount of funding they are required to raise is sufficient to implement the plan gradually.

Haimen: Female Worker Commits Suicide Due to Unemployment Caused by Illness 76

Shen Bulin, a worker at the Dasheng Third Factory in Changle Town, District 3, and his wife, Yang, worked at the factory. They had been working for several years, and their hard-earned income was enough to support them. Recently, Yang fell ill after childbirth and was laid off from work. The family's income decreased sharply, and medical expenses were high. With a family of several people, it was difficult to make ends meet. Under these circumstances, Yang felt overwhelmed by poverty and illness and developed a desire to end her life. On the morning of the 16th, she hanged herself without anyone noticing. The family discovered her and tried to rescue her, but she had been dead for a long time and could not be revived. Yesterday (the 17th), the workers at the same factory, feeling sorry for her poverty, pooled money together for a coffin and burial.

Gaoyou: Villagers Riot at the County Government for the Second Time 77

Farmers in the northeastern townships of this county rioted because they could not bear the abuse of weighing seeds during the forced labor to accumulate soil, which aroused public outrage. Yesterday (the 17th) at 10:00 AM, a group of over three thousand people gathered with farming tools and went to the city to destroy the judicial office hall, the police chief's office of the county government, and beat the secretary Sun Juexian, bailiff Yun Qi, etc. They then destroyed the first district office and the residence of Jia Fengren, the head of the construction section. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. The villagers did not leave the city and return to their villages until 10:00 PM. County Magistrate Cao returned to the city last night at 8:00 PM after receiving a telegram in Jieshou and immediately imposed martial law. All four city gates were guarded by troops, fearing that bandits would take the opportunity to infiltrate. Therefore, pedestrians were only allowed to leave the city and not enter. This morning, over a hundred farmers again gathered with small flags and rioted at the county government, trying to force their way in. Wang Yingyu, the captain of the third detachment of the provincial security team stationed in the post office, led his team to maintain order and prevent conflict. In the end, the villagers were driven out of the city. During the conflict, Wang Guangshan, a villager, had his head broken. Two strong villagers, Zhao Jinkui and Xu Zhaogen, were arrested on the spot and sent to the county for prosecution. Although the villagers have left the city, County Magistrate Cao fears that the villagers will still riot in the city, so he has closed the four city gates and prohibited traffic, cutting off transportation. He also filmed the destruction and reported it to the Provincial Government Construction Department for review.

Yang Limu, a resident of Yangjiagang, Fenghui Township, Yinxi, started his career as a farmer and accumulated some savings. Passenger on Ningxing Steamer Jumps into the Sea 81

The Ningxing Steamer of the Sanbei Company sailed from Shanghai to Ningbo the day before yesterday. The steward caught a glimpse and immediately reported it to the captain, who turned the ship back to rescue him, but he had disappeared and could not be rescued. A silk long gown, a straw hat, and a diary were found in the passenger's berth, with the name Lin Yongtang. There was a note addressed to the ship's steward, asking to send the belongings to the store, etc. There was also a wallet with a dozen business cards with the name "Lin Yongtang, Huafeng Tobacco Shop, No. 95 Seymour Road, Ningbo Zhenhai" and five yuan in banknotes, two jiao in small foreign currency, one jiao in paper money, and several photos. It is not known if he was in the photos. All the belongings have been kept by the accounting office and will be reported to the address after the ship arrives in Shanghai.

Diplomatic Envoys of Various Countries Travel by Train. Revisions to Preferential Treatment Measures. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs Seeks to Promote Friendly Relations. The Ministry of Railways Instructs All Bureaus to Comply. 83

According to the Central News Agency, in order to promote friendly relations, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has determined that the diplomatic envoys of various countries who travel to and from various places should be treated differently to show preferential treatment. After consultation with the Ministry of Railways, the Ministry of Railways agreed and issued newly revised preferential treatment measures as follows:

Instructions from the Ministry of Railways:

The Ministry of Railways has approved the letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, specifically instructing all bureaus as follows: It has been determined that the measures for the treatment of diplomatic officials stationed in China traveling on national railways were formulated by this department on April 25, 1933, and have been sent to you for reference. Now that various countries have exchanged ambassadors with our country, the treatment of ambassadors should be differentiated. The previous measures are no longer applicable. Five revised measures are hereby issued. Please check and reply.

Preferential Treatment Measures:

The newly revised preferential treatment measures include: (1) When ambassadors come to Beijing to take office or leave Beijing after their term, they may have a carriage for their use, free of charge. Train tickets are purchased at their own expense (except for the Ping-Hu through train). (2) When ministers come to Beijing to take office or leave Beijing after their term, they may reserve two compartments. Train tickets are purchased at their own expense (except for the Ping-Hu through train and the International Sleeping Car). (3) When resident charge d'affaires come to Beijing to take office or leave Beijing after their term, they may reserve one compartment. Train tickets are purchased at their own expense (except for the Ping-Hu through train and the International Sleeping Car). (4) Ambassadors, ministers, and charge d'affaires shall pay for train fare at their own expense at all times. (5) Staff members of various embassies shall pay for train fare at their own expense at all times.

American Economic Inspector Booker Returned to Shanghai Yesterday. According to Him, He Is Here to Continue Working in Shanghai. It Is Not Yet Determined Whether He Will Meet with British Expert Ross. 84

Dr. Booker, the American government's special economic investigator for China, went to Hangzhou from Shanghai a few days ago and then went to Beijing. He returned to Shanghai by train at 2:30 PM yesterday and is still staying at the Metropole Hotel on Jiangxi Road to continue his investigation work in Shanghai. He only stated that he was working on behalf of the American government and that his work was currently in progress. He was here to continue his work in Shanghai, and he could not provide any other details at this time. There was no appointment with British financial expert Ross who came to China, and it was not yet certain whether they would meet.

Tenth Anniversary of the Martyrdom of Liao Zhongkai. Representatives of All Circles Held a General Meeting Yesterday. All Institutions and Organizations Flew Flags at Half-Mast. 85

According to the Central News Agency, the tenth anniversary of the martyrdom of Mr. Liao Zhongkai, a revolutionary martyr, was commemorated. The municipal party headquarters held a memorial meeting for representatives of all circles at 9:00 AM yesterday morning. The meeting was chaired by Tong Xingbai, chairman of the municipal party committee, who reported the significance of the commemoration and ended the meeting with slogans. All institutions and organizations flew flags at half-mast for one day. Details are as follows:

Representatives Attending:

Wang Zong of the Jianghai Customs Supervisory Office, Lin Kecong of the Women's Association, Long Peiyun of the General Labor Union, Yu Yaoqiu of the Baoshan Fellow Villagers Association, Leng Xueqiao of Fudan University, Jiang Shouchun of Tongji University, Wang Zhang of the Popular Knowledge Guidance Association, Dai Yongchan of the Jiangsu Fellow Villagers Association, Wang Kegui of the Municipal Education Association, Jin Guangmei of the Women's Promotion Association, Zhu Shide of the China National Products Maintenance Association, Huang Xianggu of the Second Special Zone Citizen Association, Tong Xingbai of the Municipal Party Committee, all staff members, and representatives of various schools, totaling over one hundred people.

Chairman's Report:

After the ritual, Chairman Tong Xingbai reported that today is the tenth anniversary of the martyrdom of Liao Zhongkai, a martyr of our party. Many of Mr. Liao's achievements are worthy of our admiration. Mr. Liao grew up in the United States and returned to his native Guangdong province at the age of seventeen. By then, Mr. Liao had a foundation in Chinese studies and a considerable understanding of science. At the age of twenty-two, he married Ms. He Xiangning. However, because of Mr. Liao's great ambitions, he continued to pursue his studies, and Ms. He was able to contribute her private savings to help Mr. Liao go to Japan to study. Later, Ms. He also went to Japan, so the couple had a very deep relationship. At that time, the Russo-Japanese War broke out, and China's territory became the battlefield for the two countries. Sun Yat-sen, was saddened by the increasingly critical situation of the country. In Japan, he united comrades from seventeen provinces to organize the Chinese Tongmenghui, and Mr. and Mrs. Liao also joined. Mr. Liao originally belonged to the field of economic research, so Mr. Liao was appointed to plan finances. After the success of the Xinhai Revolution, Mr. Liao presided over the financial affairs of Guangdong province. After the failure of the campaign against Yuan Shikai in 1913, Mr. Liao followed Sun Yat-sen to Japan again to help Sun Yat-sen organize the Chinese Revolutionary Party and raise funds up to 10 million yuan. Given the environment of our party being out of power at the time, it was not easy to raise such a large sum of money. Later, the distribution of funds was very organized, which showed Mr. Liao's efforts and expertise in financial management. Later, after Yuan Shikai failed and the warlords were rampant, Mr. Liao followed Sun Yat-sen to Guangdong to prepare for the Northern Expedition. When the Northern Expedition army left Guangdong, Chen Jiongming revolted. Mr. Liao was detained for as long as sixty-two days. However, Mr. Liao did not waver in his aspirations and worked even harder for the revolutionary cause. Later, when Sun Yat-sen went to Shanghai, Mr. Liao also came and devoted himself to propaganda. He also had a book called "Politics for All," which was a great revolutionary work. In 1924, Sun Yat-sen returned to Guangdong and reorganized the Kuomintang. Mr. Liao devoted all his efforts to this and was appointed as the first Standing Committee member and Minister of the Workers' Department. However, he was deeply envied and finally assassinated by thugs at the Central Party Headquarters on this day in 1925. In Mr. Liao's life, we can observe in two aspects: In private life, he was fond of learning and never tired of it. Sun Yat-sen said that revolution is built on deep knowledge. Because Mr. Liao was fond of learning, Mr. Liao made great contributions to the revolution. In public life, Mr. Liao was loyal to the party. The morality advocated by Sun Yat-sen puts loyalty first, because the achievement of any undertaking must have an attitude of loyalty. In the past, China used loyalty to the emperor as a slogan. In the future, we should use loyalty to the country, loyalty to the people, and loyalty to the cause as slogans. Mr. Liao was relied upon for his financial management. In the past, Emperor Gaozu of Han regarded Xiao He as the most meritorious minister because he wanted to reassure the soldiers on the front line and stabilize the order in the rear, which all depended on the proper planning and operation of finance. Therefore, Mr. Liao was a great meritorious minister of our party and one of the most trusted people by Sun Yat-sen.

Memorial Slogans:

1. Mr. Liao's spirit will never die! 2. Mr. Liao is the savior of farmers and workers! 3. Learn from Mr. Liao's revolutionary spirit! 4. Relieve the suffering of farmers and workers! 5. Complete local autonomy! 6. Long live the Three Principles of the People! 7. Long live the Chinese Kuomintang!

Employer Representative to the International Labor Conference, Wang Zhisheng, Returns to Shanghai Yesterday Morning; Wang Discusses Factory Inspections and the ILO's Efforts to Resolve Issues; High Tariff Barriers Lead to Economic Decline in Various Countries 86

Wang Zhisheng, the employer representative from our country attending the 19th International Labor Conference, returned home from the United States aboard the Dollar Steamship Company's President McKinley. The ship arrived in port at 7:00 AM yesterday, docking at the Dollar Wharf in Pudong. Those welcoming him at the wharf included representatives from the Chamber of Commerce Federation, the China General Chamber of Industry, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Machinery Industry Association, Wu Wentian, a special representative sent by the Ministry of Industry, and Wang's family members, totaling more than twenty people. They departed from the Customs Wharf at 7:00 AM aboard a Dollar Steamship Company passenger boat to meet him at the Bailianjing Dollar Wharf in Pudong.

Wang Zhisheng Speaks

After exchanging greetings with the welcoming party, Wang Zhisheng spoke in detail to reporters from various newspapers about the conference and its proceedings. He stated, "This is my second time attending the International Labor Conference. This year's conference included three new member states—the United States, Russia, and Afghanistan—in addition to the seven existing member states, such as England and France, bringing the total to sixty countries. The conference took place from June 4th to June 25th. Government, labor, and employer representatives had equal standing in the conference. One of the more important proposals discussed was the working hours issue, which remained unresolved after the previous session due to strong opposition from employers. This time, it was resubmitted for reconsideration. I submitted a written opinion stating our country's position. As an employer representative, I took a proactive stance against the conference proposal, hoping to make general industrial nations aware of our country's current production situation and gain their sympathy. After intense debate among representatives from various countries, a draft for a forty-hour work week was passed. However, this is only a decision in principle, and its implementation depends on the final approval of each country's government. Furthermore, the dumping policies of various countries have a significant impact on our country's industry and commerce. This issue was raised for discussion in a subcommittee and submitted to the conference for restriction, hoping to draw the attention of various countries."

[Image of Wang Zhisheng and the welcoming party] (Photo by Zhu Shunlin)

Factory Inspections

Regarding the issue of factory inspections in concessions, our country's representatives raised the issue for discussion again. Although it was not adequately resolved, the Director of the International Labour Office, Mr. Butler, indicated that resolving factory investigations in Chinese concessions is also the responsibility of the International Labour Office. They will contact representatives from relevant countries to urge them to convey this to their respective governments and to abide by Chinese laws and be subject to Chinese inspections. Previously, representatives from England, the United States, France, Italy, and Japan were invited to a subcommittee meeting, which decided that each representative should convey this to their government and instruct their consuls in Shanghai to negotiate. Youth unemployment has become a serious problem in various countries, so the conference paid close attention to it and included it on the agenda. After detailed discussion, relief measures have been drafted.

International Labor Organization

The structure of the International Labour Organization (ILO) is becoming increasingly sound. The ILO was established after the Paris Peace Conference in 1919. The representatives from various participating countries at that time believed that in order to achieve world peace, attention should be paid not only to political issues, but also to economic and social issues. Therefore, a special section was included in the Treaty of Versailles and other treaties, stipulating the establishment of a labour organization to jointly address the solution of labour problems worldwide through international cooperation. A general assembly is held once a year, with each member state sending one labour representative, one employer representative, and two government representatives to form it. This is the highest body of the labour organization. The day-to-day affairs of the organization are handled by the International Labour Office, which is quite large in scale, with more than 500 employees. Branch offices are set up in major countries. The Governing Body of the International Labour Office serves as the supervisory body of the Labour Office, and its status is equivalent to that of the Council of the League of Nations. It has a total of thirty-two council seats, with labour and employer representatives each occupying eight seats and government representatives occupying sixteen seats. Among these sixteen seats, eight are permanently held by major industrial countries such as England and France, while the other eight seats are elected by the General Assembly every three years. Our country was elected as a director last year.

Inspection Process

After the conference closed, I went to various countries in Europe and America with Secretary Zhang Hualian to investigate industry, commerce, finance, and economics. Currently, people in Europe and America generally hold a strong hope for our country, regarding China as a peaceful country in the Far East and earnestly hoping that China can become strong externally. The economic downturn in European countries is more severe than last year. All businesses are adopting austerity policies, and the economy and finance are even more exhausted. The main reasons for this are high tariff barriers, the expansion of military spending, overproduction, and financial stagnation. After arriving in the United States, I inspected various industrial and commercial districts in New York and connected and interacted with local industrial and commercial leaders, exchanging views on promoting Sino-US industry and commerce. After the American economic inspection delegation, which previously came to China, returned to the United States, they provided detailed reports on the economic situation in various parts of our country. People in that country have a more advanced understanding of our country's industry and commerce and are eager to promote Sino-US trade in order to promote the prosperity of China's industry. This time, Secretary Zhang and I visited mints in countries such as England, the United States, France, and Belgium, and conducted a detailed investigation of these businesses. After sorting out the information during the day, I will publish it gradually to contribute to the reform of our country's currency system. Currently, Zhang is still interning at a US mint and will return to China before December of this year to serve in the Central Mint. Advisor Gu Bingyuan is still in Europe inspecting industries and is expected to return to China in the middle of next month.

Heading to the Capital Tomorrow

Wu Wentian, Section Chief of the Labour Department of the Ministry of Industry, came to Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday to represent the Ministry of Industry in welcoming Representative Wang Zhisheng. According to Wang's response to a reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency, he will stay in Beijing for a short time and then go to Beijing with Section Chief Wu the day after tomorrow to report to the Ministry. It is also reported that the local China General Chamber of Industry and other agencies and organizations will hold a banquet to welcome Wang and listen to a detailed report on his participation in the conference.

The Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces received a cable yesterday from Xu Shiying, the Vice President of the association, from Bianliang (Kaifeng): "To the President, Vice President, Directors, Deputy Directors, Secretaries-General, Deputy Secretaries-General, and all members of the Shanghai Fundraising Association for Flood Relief in Various Provinces: Numerous cables have been sent. Internal Notice Regarding the Requisition of Civilian Farmland to Develop the Yuji Mound on the Wusong River; Area Approximately 150 Acres 89

The China Society reports that the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission is requisitioning more than 150 acres of civilian farmland for the straightening and diversion of the Wusong River at Yuji Mound and the construction of a new river channel. An internal notice was specifically issued, which stated: "Approved by the National Economic Council's letter No. 4635 Shui Zi dated May 7th of the 24th year, stating, 'According to the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission's submission regarding the straightening and diversion of the Wusong River at Yuji Mound and the construction of a new river channel, it is proposed to requisition civilian farmland, with the area extending from near the Hujia Warehouse in the east to the west of the Huada Brick and Tile Factory in the west, and between the two banks of the Wusong River in the north and south, covering an area of approximately 150 acres. A joint review of the plan and the land requisition area map is requested for review and submission to the Ministry of Interior for approval.' Based on this, an investigation reveals that the Wusong River is a vital waterway for draining water from the lower reaches of Taihu Lake and a shortcut for transporting rice to Suzhou and Shanghai. It is now severely silted up, hindering drainage and navigation, particularly the excessively curved section at Yuji Mound, which is the most detrimental. The commission's plan is to first construct a new river channel in this section, straightening and diverting the river to improve the situation. This is a crucial project for the management of the Wusong River and will greatly benefit farmland and navigation. It complies with the provisions of Article 1, Item 1 and Article 2, Item 26 of the Land Requisition Law. Accordingly, in accordance with the provisions of Article 8 of the same law, the original plan and map are enclosed for review and approval for public notice.' Based on this approval, it complies with the provisions of Article 2, Item 2 and Article 6 of the Land Requisition Law and should be approved. In addition to replying for review, please proceed in accordance with the regulations. In accordance with the provisions of Article 9 of the same law, the matters to be announced are listed below for public knowledge. It is hereby announced that: (1) The responsible business entity is the National Economic Council. (2) The type of business is the development of transportation and the development of water conservancy. (3) The area of the responsible business is the Yuji Mound on the Wusong River in Shanghai, extending from near the Hujia Warehouse in the east to the west of the Huada Brick and Tile Factory in the west, and between the two banks of the Wusong River in the north and south, covering an area of approximately 150 acres of land for requisition."

Silk Merchants Organize Autumn Cocoon Purchasing Agency; 33 Silk Filatures in Shanghai Are Operational; Fear of Raw Material Shortage as Cocoon Inventory Dwindles 91

The Chinese silk industry's overseas market is gradually showing activity, with a sharp increase in exports. The price of Grade B silk has risen to 500 yuan in national currency. 33 silk filatures in Shanghai are operational. With cocoon inventory nearing depletion, silk merchants are preparing to organize an autumn cocoon purchasing agency. Details are as follows:

Overseas Trade Gradually Improves: The export trade is crucial to the Chinese silk industry. In recent years, the overseas market has been affected by the dumping of Japanese silk, leading to an oversupply of Chinese silk in the market, a significant decline in the silk weaving industry, reduced sales, and stockpiling of inventory. Silk filatures and merchants have been on the verge of bankruptcy, and most factories have ceased operations. This spring, the overseas market for Chinese silk has gradually improved. Various foreign firms in Shanghai have successively made purchases, resulting in a large number of domestic silk exports and a corresponding rise in prices.

Suspended Factories Reopen One After Another: Currently, the price of Grade B, 20-22 denier Chinese silk is approximately 500 yuan per bale (overseas) and 510 yuan per bale (domestic). This is an increase of about 100 yuan compared to the price in June. As a result, suspended factories have reopened one after another. In the four districts of Shanghai, Hongkou, Zhabei, Nanshi, and the concession, 33 silk filatures are operational, including Fu Chang, Yong Ji, Jiu Ji, Yuan Ji, Ji Yu, Hong Chang, and Xing Chang. There are 42 in Wuxi and 16 in Zhejiang. However, compared to the peak of 113 factories in Shanghai alone, this is only about one-third.

Prices Soar, Exports Surge: After prices soared, exports of Chinese silk surged. For example, in the first half of August this year, exports of Chinese silk were: (1) 1,580 bales to Europe, including 408 bales of waste silk, 5 bales of doupion silk, 76 bales of gray silk, 44 bales of yellow silk, 122 bales of Zhili silk, 99 bales of yellow filature silk, and 826 bales of white filature silk. (2) 1,731 bales to the Americas, including 104 bales of waste silk, 100 bales of gray silk, 70 bales of yellow silk, 216 bales of Zhili silk, 10 bales of yellow filature silk, and 1,231 bales of white filature silk. (3) 841 bales to India and other places, including 74 bales of white native silk, 454 bales of waste silk, 62 bales of doupion silk, 204 bales of yellow native silk, and 47 bales of white filature silk. The total is 4,152 bales.

Cocoon Inventory Dwindles, Raw Materials Scarce: Due to limited cocoon inventory, silk filatures in Shanghai are experiencing a raw material shortage panic. They are separately preparing to organize an agency to purchase autumn cocoons. However, because Zhejiang Province is implementing a unified control system, designating four districts where foreign merchants and silk merchants are allowed to purchase, the amount purchased is limited. The Shanghai Silk Filature Association has already sent a telegram to the Zhejiang Provincial Government requesting that the unified control system be lifted. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency learned from Shanghai silk filature manufacturers yesterday that they only hope that Zhejiang Province will lift the unified control system and allow Shanghai merchants to freely purchase as much as possible. Otherwise, Shanghai factories will have no raw materials to reel and will be forced to suspend operations, indirectly affecting the livelihoods of workers and having a significant impact.

New Stamp Tax Law: Relevant Provisions for Stores; The Second Special District United Association's Fourth and Fifth Branch Associations Select Provisions and Announce Them to Members for Compliance 93

Xin Xin News Agency reports that the new Stamp Tax Law has been ordered by the government to take effect on September 1st. The Fourth and Fifth Branch Associations of the Second Special District Citizens' United Association have resolved through the Executive Committee to select relevant provisions for stores from the new Stamp Tax Law and announce them to their members for uniform compliance. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency has transcribed the announcement and provisions as follows:

Notice to Members

For the purpose of notification, the new Stamp Tax Law has been ordered by the government to take effect on September 1st of this year. In order to ensure that members comply, the association has resolved through the Executive Committee to select relevant provisions for stores from the new Stamp Tax Law and announce them to the members for uniform compliance. Therefore, the attached provisions are for your attention and compliance. This is specifically announced. Right to all members, from the Fourth and Fifth Branch Associations of the Second Special District Citizens' United Association of Shanghai.

New Stamp Tax

Attached are relevant provisions on tax rates from Chapter Two of the new Stamp Tax Law: (1) Invoices; (2) Receipts for money, goods, and merchandise; (3) Bills - Each item with an amount (or value) of 3 yuan or more requires a stamp worth 1 fen. Those with 10 yuan and above require a stamp of 2 fen. Those with 100 yuan and above require a stamp of 3 fen. (4) Vouchers or ledgers for withdrawing or remitting money (vouchers or ledgers for withdrawing or remitting money issued by public professional institutions or ledgers used by workers in various industries to withdraw wages are exempt from stamps); (5) Vouchers or ledgers for withdrawing goods; (6) Vouchers or contracts for pre-ordered purchase of goods; (7) Vouchers or ledgers used for managing the sale of valuable securities and raw gold, silver, or goods - each voucher requires a stamp of 2 fen, each ledger requires a stamp of 1 jiao per year, and each contract requires a stamp of 2 jiao. Vouchers for each item with a value of less than 3 yuan are exempt. (8) Deposit receipts; (9) Savings receipts - each item requires a stamp of 2 fen. (10) Lease receipts or contracts (if rent is collected using ledgers, stamps should be affixed according to the example of the fourth type of ledgers) - each item requires a stamp of 2 fen. Leases with an amount of less than 10 yuan are exempt. (11) Books used for business - each book requires a stamp of 2 jiao per year.

Post Office Unnecessary Display of On-Duty Personnel Names: Discussions with Standing Committee Members of the Postal Workers' Unions 98

Yesterday's newspaper reported a post office notice stating that post office employees should be humble and disciplined, and treat people with kindness. They would be implementing the display of office hours and the names of on-duty personnel to facilitate public interaction, etc. Yesterday, standing committee members of the Shanghai Postal Workers' Unions told a visitor that the post office has been established for more than thirty years and has never displayed the names of on-duty employees, yet employees have never treated the public with an unkind attitude. Moreover, if there are any complaints from the outside world about any postal employee, the postal authorities have always been able to investigate and impose appropriate punishment. Therefore, the implementation of this method of displaying the names of on-duty employees is superfluous. Furthermore, the Telegraph Bureau, Radio Station, and other state-run transportation agencies do not display employee names; they only use numbers to represent them. Since postal and telecommunications bureaus are in the same position and are governed by the same superior authority, such differences should not exist. Postal employees strongly oppose this method and have already requested that the Ministry revoke the order. At the very least, they should be allowed to use numbers instead, as is the practice at the Telegraph Bureau. Although the post office has already implemented the display of names, employees are still awaiting the final instructions from the Ministry of Transportation.

Luo Qinghua presided over the meeting, and after formal greetings, the chairman gave an opening address and reported on the association's activities. After the Economics Section reported on the financial situation, Chairman Luo Qinghua reported on the progress of promoting commercial acceptance bills. He stated that our silk and satin industry has traditionally relied on the silver and money shops for financing customer credit transactions. This practice has been in place for a long time. However, the silver and money shops are now tightening credit, leading to a depletion of resources and a difficult situation. Purely cash transactions are not easily reformed due to ingrained habits, and economic hardship is widespread. Customers everywhere cannot escape this situation. Therefore, changing the credit system to cash transactions is not feasible. In order to consider the interests of both buyers and sellers, the association believes that the use of commercial acceptance bills is the most appropriate solution. After several discussions with legal counsel and accountants, it was determined that this is in accordance with the new Negotiable Instruments Law promulgated by the Legislative Yuan. It was resolved to submit this proposal to the General Meeting for approval and to implement it simultaneously with the Electrical Machinery and Silk Weaving Industry Association from April 1st. Subsequently, because customers still did not fully understand the meaning and benefits of these bills, we invited representatives from the traveling salesmen to a joint meeting. It was resolved to have each representative organize a Commercial Acceptance Bill Promotion Committee to explain the process to each guild. It was also resolved to promote the procedure, starting with the Guangdong and Ningbo guilds as models for other guilds. At that time, those two guilds were hesitant and waited to see what would happen. After the representatives explained the situation and Qinghua personally contacted them, the Xulun Da Tong Hang and the Guangdong guild responded one after another, agreeing to comply. However, the Guangdong guild had some reservations regarding the time frame. The length of time and the number of bills could be negotiated by both the buyer and seller, which should not be a problem. During this time, the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau issued an order promoting the effort, and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and the Silver and Money Shops Association actively promoted it. Leaders and economic experts from all walks of life recognized that these acceptance bills were a credit tool that met the needs of the times and could alleviate the current economic difficulties. Therefore, various industries have followed suit. The industry has taken the lead in creating these bills, and all members have long been aware of their benefits, but they are still not widely used. This is due to the difficulty of changing old habits and a lack of self-motivation, which is regrettable. It must be understood that we are facing an unprecedented economic crisis, and we must work together to become self-reliant. Eliminating malpractices and innovating requires collective efforts and concerted progress to succeed. If we hesitate and wait, even good policies will be ineffective and we will inevitably perish. The promotion of these bills is simply a modification of the existing credit system, with the aim of increasing the turnover of the industry's capital while not hindering the convenience of each guild. If it can be universally implemented, it will not only alleviate the current economic panic but also greatly benefit the future development of industry and commerce. Financial leaders also believe that in this time of tight credit and increased panic, only the automatic creation of credit tools by the industry can save the situation. Therefore, they are happy to provide assistance and allow for acceptance and discounting of these bills. The Central Bank has also authorized commercial banks to rediscount them. Recently, the banking industry has begun to organize an acceptance house and is about to start issuing bank acceptance bills. Therefore, our colleagues in the association should strengthen their beliefs, continue their efforts, and complete the promotion of these acceptance bills to benefit the industry significantly. The next item was a discussion of proposals: (1) The Current Affairs Committee proposed that the government should reward foreign trade and properly determine the method for refunding raw material taxes on national silk. Resolution: Passed. (2) Luo Qinghua proposed that the government should establish a domestic artificial silk factory to prevent leakage and maintain the industry. Resolution: Passed. (3) Wang Zuyin proposed that a large sum of money should be raised for a large-scale national silk promotion campaign to awaken the attention of the people and save the decline of national silk. Resolution: Passed in principle, to be discussed by the Executive Committee. Subsequently, representatives from the Party Department and the Chamber of Commerce gave speeches, expressing their appreciation. The speeches were lengthy and are not recorded here.

Autumn Fishing Season: Fish Market Ready to Open 100

The fish market, built by the Ministry of Industry with one million yuan at the end of Shupu Road, north of Dinghai Bridge along the river, has been under construction since December of last year. Nine months have passed, and it is scheduled to open for business during the autumn fishing season. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited the market yesterday to inspect the progress of the construction. The details are as follows:

Total Construction to be Completed in a Month

The fish market is located on the bank of the Huangpu River, between the city center and the International Settlement, covering an area of approximately forty acres. The buildings include a three-story office building with a three-story observation tower on top, an auction hall, dozens of offices for brokers, and a cold storage facility and a water tower. All are constructed of copper and reinforced concrete. In addition, the market has wide gravel roads throughout, providing convenient transportation to all areas. Currently, all buildings except the water tower are largely completed. The entire project is expected to be completed in a month.

Wharf along the River is Currently Piling

Along the river, a 601-foot area is currently being constructed with a bank and five wharves for the future docking and unloading of fishing boats. From the wharf, there are warehouses for unloading goods. The wharf is currently being piled and is still far from being usable.

Pin Zhen Jewelry Store Accused of Tax Evasion: Trial Begins: Customs Records Show Pin Zhen Did Not Import Goods: Court Approves Provision of Security to Avoid Seizure of Goods 105

Pin Zhen Jewelry Store, located at 639 Nanjing Road, was found by the Jianghai Customs to be suspected of tax evasion. Customs officials, along with police officers, raided the store on the 12th of this month and seized diamond jewelry worth 70,000 to 80,000 yuan, which was then handed over to the First Special District Court for detention. This has been reported in this newspaper. The police station, in accordance with Article 21 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations, filed a public prosecution against the store's manager, Dong Shuyu. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhan Liangce of the First Special Court held a hearing in the Second Criminal Court. Dong Shuyu hired Fan Gang, Qin Liankui, and Ni Jiong as lawyers for defense. The police lawyer, Zhang Shizhu, stated that the Jianghai Customs had imported diamonds worth 17,736.11 yuan in customs gold, totaling 35,000 national currency, since 1920. However, Pin Zhen's imports this year alone have reached more than 40,000 yuan, exceeding the total imports by customs for the past five years by more than 6,000 yuan. The police also found two letters dated February 8 and March 14 of this year in the Pin Zhen store, both of which mentioned purchasing diamonds from Bombay, India. They also found eight telegrams, all related to remittances to Bombay, with very large amounts. However, there are no records of diamond imports by Pin Zhen in the customs records, indicating that they were indeed evading taxes. The police are continuing their investigation and request that the hearing be adjourned. When questioned, Dong Shuyu stated that all the letters and telegrams did not belong to the store. Pin Zhen was reorganized last year, and these items may have been left by the previous owners. Of the goods imported this year, more than 20,000 yuan were purchased from Uliwen, Buxing, Maji, and Beilaiheng Foreign Firms, and the rest were purchased from other companies in the market. According to jewelery industry practice, there are no receipts for these, and he submitted a letter from the Jewelery Industry Association to prove this. His lawyer, in accordance with Article 6 of the Anti-Smuggling Regulations, requested that the defendant be allowed to provide sufficient security to have the goods returned first. Judge Zhan, after reviewing the evidence, ordered the case to be adjourned because further investigation was needed. If the defendant could provide a security deposit of 75,000 yuan, the seized items would not be detained.

Shi Guoliang, Accomplice in Corpse Destruction Case, Transferred: Shi Admits Being at the Scene but Denies Pushing the Body: Brought Back by Municipal Public Security Bureau for Questioning 106

At 2 PM on the 10th of this month, Lu Genji Motor Transport Company, which was transporting bricks and tiles, had driver Jiang Asi drive a truck with four workers and the company's accountant, Shi Guoliang, to the Xiaoyang Bridge area of Jiaotong Road in Zhabei. Due to speeding, the truck accidentally hit and injured a pedestrian, Mr. Jia, who died on the spot. Jiang Asi and the others, realizing that they had caused an accident, had malicious intentions and attempted to move the body to destroy evidence. They lifted the deceased onto the truck, drove straight to Kuizhao Road in Jiangwan, pushed the body off, and drove away quickly, hoping that no one would know about the incident and they could evade responsibility. However, the Municipal Central District Public Security Bureau learned of the incident and detained several workers, including Hou Guisheng, and brought them to the bureau for questioning. Hou confessed that the accountant, Shi Guoliang, was hiding at 426 Alabaster Road. The Central District Public Security Bureau sent Detective Wang Yao, along with detectives from the Foreign Concession Police Station, to arrest Shi Guoliang. However, Jiang Asi was on the run. Shi was taken into custody at the police station. Yesterday morning, he was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, presented the case, stating that this was an accessory case and that it was located with the help of the accomplice Hou Guisheng. An unidentified male corpse was found on Kuizhao Road in Jiangwan, who was found to have been crushed to death by a car. It was learned that at 2 PM on the 10th of this month, a truck from Lu Genji Motor Transport Company, with Foreign Concession license No. 16054 and Municipal license No. 12014, was driven by driver Jiang Asi to Jiaotong Road in Zhabei. Due to speeding, the truck hit a pedestrian. In addition to the driver Jiang Asi, the respondent Shi Guoliang and four workers were on the truck. They initially intended to send the injured person to the hospital, but he died as soon as they lifted him onto the truck. They then changed their plan and attempted to move the body to destroy evidence, throwing the body on Kuizhao Road in Jiangwan. He added that it should be questioned as to who did push the body. Then, accomplice Hou Guisheng testified that he was a worker on the truck that day. After hitting the pedestrian on Jiaotong Road, they lifted the injured person onto the truck and drove to a certain road in Jiangwan, where driver Jiang Asi and Shi Guoliang pushed the body off. When questioned, Shi Guoliang only admitted to being on the truck that day and denied pushing the body. Detective Wang Yao from the Central District Public Security Bureau then requested to take over the case for further investigation, and the police lawyer did not object. Judge Wu Zehan approved Shi Guoliang's transfer to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning.

Changes in Reconciliation Terms for China Industrial Bank: Lu Xihou Sues Judge for Loss of Documents: Lawsuits Breed Lawsuits in This Entangled Case: Unprecedented Incident Arouses Great Concern from All Parties 107

After the China Industrial Bank collapsed on the day after the Double Tenth Festival last year, the bank's chairman, Lu Xihou, was prosecuted by the police station in the First Special District Court on charges of fraud and embezzlement. After repeated investigations, the court ruled to suspend the public prosecution and instructed Lu, in the name of the legal representative of the China Industrial Bank, to file a petition to liquidate all of the bank's accounts. The case was then transferred from the Criminal Court to the Civil Court, and Judge Yu Changzi of the Civil Court was assigned to handle the case. For several months, Judge Yu held several court sessions, summoning witnesses from both creditors and debtors for careful examination. Eventually, the parties reached a settlement out of court and proposed a settlement plan, which generally stipulated that the bank's debts, in addition to being repaid with the bank's assets, would be the responsibility of Lu Xihou to handle the shortfall. Lu then submitted the plan to the court for approval. However, Lu recently learned that the notice issued by the court to the creditors regarding the settlement plan contained descriptions of the settlement terms that were very different from those submitted to the court, with significant discrepancies. Therefore, Lu believed that the judge in charge of the case had acted improperly, causing him to suffer damages, and he could not remain silent. He has now filed a petition with the First Special Court to reclaim criminal jurisdiction. The reorganization of the formal court in the recovery of the law rights has never been seen in the past few years. What has happened today is the first time, and all parties are paying extraordinary attention to it. The Bureau of Public Works is particularly concerned and will send personnel to the court to record the proceedings during the public hearing. However, the parties involved do not want to expand the incident and hope that it can be resolved peacefully before the court hearing. However, after the court received Lu's complaint, it issued a summons, ordering the staff of the Hongkou police station, who are responsible for self-accusations, to send police officers to deliver the summons to the parties involved, ordering them to appear in court on time to defend themselves.

Lu Ruifang Requests Restoration of Father-Son Relationship: Leaves as a Child, Regrets as an Adult: Mediation Fails, Formal Lawsuit Filed 108

Lu Weirong, the chief comprador of Jardine Matheson & Co., is a native of Ningbo Cixi and is over sixty years old. He lives at No. 5 Mingyu Lane, Jing'an Temple Road. He often contributes generously to charitable causes. Lu's first wife died of illness twenty-seven years ago, leaving behind a son named Ruifang, who is now thirty-five years old. However, Lu has another concubine, with whom he has two sons and one daughter, all of whom have grown up and married. However, the relationship between Lu Ruifang and his father, Weirong, is not very harmonious. Therefore, after Ruifang married in September of his eighteenth year, father and son clashed less than four months later and argued fiercely. On the eighth day of December of that year, Ruifang, unable to tolerate his father, took his wife out and rented a house elsewhere. In January of the following year, Lu's relatives came forward to draw up a severance agreement, and Lu Weirong published a statement in the newspaper, severing the father-son relationship with Ruifang. Since then, for more than ten years, father and son have had no contact. Recently, Lu Ruifang, due to his longing for his father, and because he was not yet an adult when the severance agreement was signed, hired lawyer Jia Yaoxi to file a petition with the First Special District Court for mediation, requesting the restoration of the father-son relationship and the cancellation of the severance agreement. Since then, father and son have been estranged. For more than ten years, the applicant has longed to serve his father and enjoy his love, but has been unsuccessful. Therefore, he has no choice but to seek legal remedy to restore the relationship between flesh and blood, restore the father-son relationship, and declare the illegal documents signed by the applicant during his minority to be invalid. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang presided over the mediation of the case in the Eleventh Civil Court. As a result, the mediation failed, and the judge ordered a formal lawsuit.

A Tragic Incident: One Life Lost Due to a Bench Blow – Two Apprentice Students in a Major Dispute Cause a Great Calamity – A Bench Breaks a Skull, Resulting in Instant Death 111

Zhang Degui, a Yangzhou native, recently opened a rubber-soled shoe workshop at No. 52, Lujiabang Road, south of Malu Bridge in the southern part of the city. His business was quite prosperous, and he employed many partners and apprentices, including Zhu Deqing (18 years old) and Ni Zhongxin (19 years old), both from Yangzhou. These two were usually fond of playing and joking with each other, making it a common occurrence. One day before yesterday, around 7 PM, while they were having supper, because Zhang Degui, the shop owner, was out, Zhu Deqing, Ni Zhongxin, and others started another dispute. A tragic scene unfolded then and there. The other partners didn't think much of it. Unexpectedly, Ni Zhongxin kept nagging, and Zhu Deqing, being young and impetuous and of a rash disposition, picked up a bench and used it as a weapon. It hit Ni's nose. Ni, after being struck, became enraged. He seized the bench from Zhu Deqing's hand and struck Zhu Deqing's head in retaliation. Because he used excessive force, Zhu's skull was shattered, and he was injured. He immediately fell to the ground, his face turned pale, and he had only a faint breath. Soon, he died. The fellow partners, witnessing the great calamity, were all astonished. They immediately seized the assailant Ni Zhongxin and handed him over to the police on duty, who took him to the Wenmiao Road Police Station for temporary detention. Yesterday morning, Tao Yong, the 27th Ward bailiff, reported to the local court, requesting an autopsy. After receiving the report, the court immediately sent prosecutor Lei Binzhang, along with examiner Xuan Zhiming, to the scene to conduct the examination. They confirmed that Zhu Deqing had died from a fractured skull. They filled out the coroner's report and ordered Zhang Degui, the shop owner, to arrange the coffin and burial, pending the police station's interrogation and legal proceedings against the suspect Ni Zhongxin. It is said that the deceased's family is in their hometown of Yangzhou, with his father alive and his mother deceased, along with a young brother. Zhang Degui, the shop owner, has sent a letter urging the deceased's father to come to Shanghai to take care of everything.

At this time, when the hotel industry relies heavily on gifts to promote business, we dare to ask your company to promote our assembly's tour tickets, either by giving them as gifts to customers or by selling them on our behalf. Not only will your company's business develop further, but also the benefits to the disaster victims will be significant. It is truly a win-win situation. We believe your company will be happy to agree. Therefore, we are sending you tour tickets and hope that you will promote them or give them away to support this grand event. We look forward to your cooperation."

Yesterday's Sultry Thunderstorm – The Weather Cooled Down and Cleared Up 116

The climate in this city has been most sultry since the beginning of autumn yesterday morning. In the morning, the red sun was in the sky, and the business of cold drinks everywhere was very good. By a little after 3 PM, suddenly dark clouds gathered, and thunder rumbled. Within moments, a torrential downpour occurred. It stopped after half an hour. Before long, another shower fell. At 4:30 PM, the clouds dispersed, the rain stopped, a cool breeze blew, and the sky cleared up, making one feel refreshed.
