Chen Xichu Drowns While Swimming in Minhang – A Promising Young Man Dies Tragically 119

Chen Xiting's eldest son, Chen Xichu, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Citizens' Association for the Promotion of National Products and a passenger on the state-owned China Merchants Bureau's Xinjiangfutian Steamer, was a handsome and intelligent young man with outstanding academic achievements. After graduating from Qingxin Middle School two years ago, he showed great promise and had strong patriotic ideals. He was determined to study chemistry in depth, manufacture national products, save the country through production, and plug the leaks in our economy. He studied with Dr. Ye Hancheng, the director of the Wuzhou Gubend Soap Factory, and entered the factory as an intern. He had been there for three years, working diligently and gaining much knowledge. He was striving hard and achieving excellent results, earning the praise of his teacher and the admiration of his colleagues, and showing the glory of surpassing his predecessors. Last Sunday, as usual, he rested. Feeling the heat of the autumn tiger and the stuffiness of the city air, he invited his three colleagues, Qin Zhenqiu, _ Yuchun, and Shi Fuling, to ride bicycles west to get some fresh air. They first went to the Huang Family Garden in Caohejing for a short rest and then continued bravely until they stopped at Minhang Pubin Garden. Chen Xichu was fond of swimming. Seeing the refreshing west wind by the sea and the waves like a clear mirror, he was so excited that he immediately changed into his swimsuit and jumped into the water. Unexpectedly, he was stirred up by an evil tide and lost control. His colleagues were young and even more unfamiliar with swimming. They called for help, but he had already sunk to the bottom of the river. By the time he was fished out and brought ashore, there were no good facilities. It would be impossible to get a doctor from Shanghai and back within several hours. By the time the doctor arrived in Minhang, it was too late to save him. He died tragically, a handsome young man. Alas! Chen Xichu was only 21 years old. His relatives and friends were all grieved. However, his teacher, Mr. Ye Hancheng, wept even more bitterly. His body was transported back to Shanghai and laid in a coffin at the Dinghai Guild Hall. It is said that Chen's relatives, friends, and Chen Xichu's classmates will launch a memorial service to comfort his soul.

Zhou A'da Tragically Drowns 121

Zhou A'da, a 46-year-old boatman from Changshu, was sailing his boat near the Fuxin Flour Mill on Suzhou Road the day before yesterday. Due to the rapid currents, Luo Laiqing's pig boat and Gao Liansheng's watermelon boat approached and collided with Zhou A'da's boat. Zhou A'da was standing on the bow of the boat. Because he was not paying attention, he was knocked into the river. He did not surface and drowned. The neighboring boats tried to search for him in all directions but found nothing. As a result, the body was recovered and temporarily placed on the river beach. Anhui Woman Liu Ying Attempts Suicide in the River – A Beautiful Story from the Gallery – A Pitiable Background Arouses Sympathy from All Sides – Willingness to Adopt Leads to Mrs. Chen's Good Fortune 122

Liu Ying, a 20-year-old woman from Anhui, lost her mother when she was six years old. Six years ago, when she graduated from the Junior High School Department of Anhui Provincial First Girls' Middle School, her father also passed away due to illness. Liu, because of her poor family background, was unable to continue her education. She dropped out of school and became a primary school teacher in her hometown, using her income to support herself and her younger brother and sister. Liu has an elder sister named Manli, who married years ago and lives with her husband in Nanjing. Her brother-in-law is currently working in the political circles in Nanjing. During the winter vacation last year, Liu Ying felt that she had been living in her hometown for too long and it was difficult to achieve a better life and make progress. She packed her bags, said goodbye to her brother and sister, and came to Shanghai alone, intending to visit her old friend Lin Yuying, hoping to ask her for a job. Unexpectedly, when Liu arrived in Shanghai, Lin had already gone to Nanyang and they did not meet. Liu was greatly disappointed. Liu had no relatives or friends in Shanghai to turn to. If she returned to her hometown, it would be a futile and arduous journey. Seeing that Shanghai was a prosperous commercial city, she thought that if she waited for an opportunity, she could always find a position. Therefore, she stayed at the Shanghai Women's Apartment at the entrance of Sande Lane, Bubo Road in the French Concession, waiting for an opportunity. Who knew that after coming to Shanghai for half a year, she had asked around everywhere but found nothing. The money she had brought was also exhausted, and she owed the apartment for room and board, which she could not pay. Frustrated and helpless, she was pushed to despair and had the idea of suicide. So, the day before yesterday (the 19th) at 8 PM, Liu Ying walked to the French Company Wharf on the Bund and jumped into the river to kill herself. At that time, there were many people at the pier who witnessed Liu Ying jumping into the river and were shocked. They shouted for help. The boatmen next to the pier helped with the rescue. They used a pole to pull Liu Ying up as she floated after jumping down, and handed her over to the patrol police on the shore, who took her to the French Police Station for questioning and temporary detention. Yesterday morning, the police station ordered detectives to take Liu Ying to the Special Second Court to request instructions. At 11 o'clock, Judge Qiu Huanying came to the Criminal Court Eight to question her. First, lawyer Yao Zhaodi from the Police Department stated Liu Ying's rescue after attempting suicide and requested instructions on how to settle her. When Liu Ying walked into the courtroom, her face was full of sorrow, and she tearfully recounted her arrival in Shanghai, her life experiences, and her misfortunes. The judge advised her, "Suicide is the most painful and cowardly strategy in life. You should strive forward to seek progress." Liu replied, "I have been striving all along, but the result is always that there is no way out." During the interrogation in court, the audience was moved and felt sympathy for Liu. Lawyer Yao Zhaodi of the Police Department also asked Liu if she had taken the examination for primary school teachers before. Liu replied that when she was a teacher, there was no such regulation for examination. At this point, lawyer Yao indicated that he could find someone to arrange a suitable position for Liu. It was imperative to find a way to support Liu's life in the near future. At that time, a Ms. Chen in the audience heard Liu's pitiable background and felt compassion. She stood up and told the court that she was willing to temporarily adopt Liu. The judge then called Chen to the front of the case and asked her about her address and occupation. After questioning, Liu also expressed her consent. Liu then left with Ms. Chen.

There were also four other victims: apprentice Lu Lianbao, (18 years old, place of origin unknown,) laborer Chen Yuanjin from Changzhou, (27 years old,) Chen Xikang from Chongming, (18 years old,) and iron worker Xue Jinsheng from Wuxi, (52 years old,) who were injured in the head, hands, or feet. They were sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment. Lu and the two Chens suffered relatively minor injuries. However, the iron worker Xue Jinsheng was more seriously injured and remained in the hospital for treatment.

Bad Check to Obtain Rice – Hu Mingzhen Blames Jin Juren 127

Jin Juren, the manager of the Fuxinggong Rice Shop on Dajing Road, Xiaobeimen, had a customer named Hu Mingzhen, who lived at No. 224, Qinglian Lane, Qinglian Street, purchase seven loads of white rice a week ago, totaling eighty-odd dollars. He ordered the shop to deliver the rice and collect the payment. Because the rice needed to be weighed and the quality of the rice needed to be inspected, Jin ordered the shop clerk to deliver the rice, as Qinglian Lane was nearby. After Hu Mingzhen inspected and accepted the rice, he paid with a Tai Kang Zhuang bank draft dated August 18th and told the shop clerk that if the shop needed cash, they could discount the draft at the bank. Therefore, Jin Juren did not suspect anything. When the draft matured, he submitted it to the Xing Shanghai Bank for collection, but the Tai Kang Zhuang had already gone bankrupt and the draft was returned. Jin immediately went to Hu Mingzhen to demand payment, but Hu replied that he had already told the shop clerk to discount the draft immediately. He further claimed that the shop did not collect the payment on the 18th, but waited until the 19th, when the bank had already gone bankrupt. Hu refused to take responsibility and blamed Jin's company for the delay. However, Jin had already investigated and found that Tai Kang Zhuang had gone bankrupt long ago. As a result of the dispute, the police were called and they were taken to the Laobeimen Police Station for investigation. After questioning by Chief Shen, it was determined that the case involved a bad bank draft used to defraud food rice. The case was referred to the General Bureau for investigation and handling.

Red Swastika Society: Investigation Report on the Yangtze River Disaster 132

Following the occurrence of floods in various provinces along the Yangtze River, the general and branch societies of the Red Swastika Society immediately dispatched teams to the disaster areas for relief. At the same time, Li Cikai (Digguang) was publicly appointed as the representative of Chairman Wang Weiguan, and Xu Boquan as the representative of Chairman Zhou Zongliang, to lead staff members to the disaster areas along the river to conduct on-site investigations. The society has now received detailed reports of the disaster situation from the two special commissioners, Li and Xu. Excerpts are as follows: (Omitted above) In the counties near Wuhu, a vast expanse of water submerged all the ripe crops. The breached dikes were mostly small and medium-sized dikes. Larger dikes were fortunately preserved due to effective emergency protection. In Guanzhuang Dike in Tongling County, over 40,000 mu of farmland were breached and completely submerged, leaving 50,000 to 60,000 disaster victims without clothing or food, crying for help. In the Guangcheng Dike area of Anqing, many disaster victims gathered in makeshift reed sheds, suffering from hunger and disease, their cries of misery unbearable to hear. Furthermore, the Ma Hua Dike on Madang Mountain, at the border of Jiangxi and Anhui, collapsed, turning Susong and Wangjiang counties into watery realms. Anhui Province has suffered from drought and banditry for years, leaving many homes empty. Now, it has been hit by this great disaster, with all the ripe crops submerged. Alas, our compatriots will have nowhere to die. Traveling upstream, inspections along the north bank of the river revealed that eight out of ten dikes had been breached. The south bank, with its mountains and higher terrain, suffered less damage. This flood was initially caused by a downpour in Shaanxi, which flowed down to Jianli, causing the Xiang River to overflow and inundate the area from Xiangyang to Hanyang. In one day and night, several counties were submerged, with hundreds of thousands of people drowned, a truly unbearable tragedy. In the flood of the 20th year, the downstream was severely affected, while the upstream was less so. This year's flood, however, is extremely severe upstream and less so downstream. The team traveled by small boat along the Xiang River to Tianmen, passing through Caidian in Hanyang and reaching Hanchuan. There were dozens of breaches along the river. Climbing to the high ground in Hanchuan County, one could see nothing but water, as if standing outside Wusongkou and gazing at the ocean. This is the area bordering Tianmen County. As for Tianmen, Yicheng, Xiangyang, and Fancheng, all were covered in white waves, with extremely severe disaster conditions, truly a catastrophe. In total, 300,000 people in Hanyang, Hanchuan, and Tianmen counties cannot survive without relief, and 200,000 people in Xiangyang, Yicheng, and Zhongxiang counties cannot survive without help. Currently, the Wuhan Red Swastika Society has organized a relief office for the Hubei flood and, in conjunction with Red Swastika Societies and charitable organizations in various places, has already distributed 70,000 to 80,000 yuan for emergency relief. The society's relief team is still distributing emergency relief in Hanyang, under the leadership of Chairman He Hengfu, in cooperation with local flood relief organizations, dividing labor and coordinating efforts appropriately based on the urgency of the situation. The 4,000 bags of relief flour transported by the society will arrive in Hankou within a few days, and various medicines have also been received and distributed to the disaster areas for relief. Plans are now underway to provide emergency relief to the most severely affected areas in Xiangyang, Tianmen, and Fancheng. Broad beans are considered the most suitable relief grain, priced at 2.67 yuan per hundred catties. However, this is only a drop in the bucket and cannot solve the problem. It is hoped that more funds can be raised to save the people from disaster. It is also reported that the Southeast Joint Office of the society has scheduled a meeting of representatives from various provinces in Shanghai on the 22nd of this month to discuss relief methods.

Compilation of Bank Inspection Reports 136

The 244th inspection report on the issuance reserve of the Central Bank's convertible notes states: In accordance with Article 13 of the Central Bank Law, the association is responsible for inspecting the amount of convertible notes issued by the bank and the reserve fund. The 244th inspection was conducted at the bank's issuing department on August 17, 1945. The results of the inspection are reported as follows: A. The total amount of convertible notes issued is 109,541,613 silver dollars, including 102,539,743 silver dollar notes and 7,001,870 subsidiary currency notes. The total amount of the convertible note reserve is 84,781,613 silver dollars in gold reserve. This cash reserve includes 79,602,136 yuan stored in the bank's issuing vault, 2,166,316 yuan stored in branch offices in various ports, and 3,013,161 yuan deposited with correspondent banks. The security reserve is equivalent to 24,760,000 silver dollars. B. The total amount of customs gold convertible notes issued is 373,324.70 yuan. The total amount of customs gold convertible note reserve is 373,324.70 yuan. This reserve includes 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, equivalent to 373,324.70 customs gold at a fixed price of 50,779. According to Article 22 of the Central Bank Law, the cash reserve must be at least 60 percent, with the remainder being legal securities as a security reserve. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60 percent, and the security reserve is within 40 percent, which complies with the regulations. This report is hereby submitted. August 19, 1945, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, Supervisors Xie Mengjun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Qia Yuqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jili

The Four Banks Reserve, jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jin Cheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks, specializes in issuing Zhongnan Bank banknotes. In accordance with the bank's issuing charter, banknotes are issued with a 100% reserve. The cash reserve is at least 60%, and the security reserve is at most 40%. It is announced once a week after verification by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The 294th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve on August 17, 1945, is recorded as follows: The amount of banknotes in circulation is 19,142,073 yuan. The total amount of the reserve fund is 19,142,073 yuan, including a cash reserve of 16,791,693 yuan and a security reserve of 2,350,380 yuan.

Chinese Physical Education Society: Drafted Articles of Association and Prepared for Establishment; General Assembly Scheduled for October 143

The Chinese Physical Education Society, initiated by Cheng Dengke, Shao Rugan, Wu Bangwei, Zhang Dongping, Jiang Lianggui, and many others in the sports circles of Beijing and Shanghai, has appointed Shao Rugan and Zhang Dongping to draft the articles of association and prepare for its establishment. A general assembly is scheduled to be held in Shanghai during the opening of the National Games. The draft articles of association are excerpted below: (1) Name: The society is named the Chinese Physical Education Society. (2) Purpose: The society is a purely academic research organization with the purpose of studying physical education. (3) Membership: A. Any organization that is willing to study and promote physical education may become a group member of the society after being reviewed and approved by the board of directors and submitted to the general assembly for approval. Group members pay an annual fee of 10 yuan and have the right to send people to vote and be elected as directors of the society, as well as to enjoy all publications issued by the society. B. Any individual who is willing to study and promote physical education may become a member of the society after being introduced by two or more members and approved by the board of directors. Individual members pay an annual fee of 2 yuan or a one-time fee of 20 yuan as permanent members. They have the right to be elected as directors of the society and receive all publications of the society. (4) Staff: A. The board of directors of the society is composed of 12 individual members and three group members, who are responsible for all society affairs. One-third of the board of directors is re-elected by mail every year. They may be re-elected for consecutive terms. The details will be determined separately. B. The society has three standing directors, who are mutually elected by the directors to manage all internal and external affairs of the society. C. All staff members of the society are honorary positions and are not paid salaries, except for those specially hired. (5) Organization: The society has a general office, a translation department, a research department, a promotion department, and a physical education book and newspaper circulation department. Member services will be determined separately. (6) Work: Organize physical education seminars, physical education academic lectures, edit annual reports and other publications related to physical education, and establish a physical education circulation library. (7) Meetings: The society's meetings are divided into the following three types: A. The society holds a general assembly once a year, convened by the board of directors. B. The board of directors discusses all matters related to the society's progress, convened by the chairman of the standing committee. C. The society may convene extraordinary meetings by the board of directors when necessary. (8) Branches: If there are more than 20 members of the society in any location, they may form a branch. The charter will be determined separately. (9) Supplementary Provisions: Matters not covered in this charter may be proposed by 18 or more members of the society and amended by a resolution of the general assembly, and reported to the competent education administrative agency for record.

Hangzhou Mayor's Changfeng Team Attempts to Cross the Qiantang River 145

(Hangzhou News) The Hangzhou Mayor's Changfeng Swimming Association held a demonstration swim across the Qiantang River yesterday (the 18th). Before 10 AM, they gathered at the riverside bathing area. Director Xu of the Provincial Education Department, Mayor Zhou, the Provincial Government Secretary-General and his wife, and over a hundred guests all went to observe. At 11 AM, they hired a boat to the Jiangbian Head in Changhe, Xiaoshan, on the opposite bank. At 11:48:40, Zhu Jia issued the command to enter the water. Eleven people participated in the crossing. Zhu provided guidance beforehand, emphasizing the swift downstream currents and instructing Yu Shujian and Zhou Zhaohua to accompany the team members on the left and right sides, respectively, to prevent any unforeseen circumstances. After hearing the command, the participants entered the water. Initially, there was no clear separation, but after a period of swimming, positions began to emerge. Zhou Zhaohua showed great courage and led the group, setting an example for young swimmers like Ding Naixing, who also strived to follow closely behind, battling the river currents, moving straight without veering, and thus Zhou and others were the first to reach the finish line. The entire course, totaling 1,100 meters, was completed in 19 minutes and 20 seconds. Ding Naixing, Huang Guangrun, Tang Yunzhong, Qian Yunnan, Yao Jinli, Yang Bingfu, and others arrived successively. Yu Shujian and Chen Zhiqing, carried downstream by the current, circled the river surface near the Six Harmonies Pagoda before returning to the riverside bathing area, covering a total distance of approximately 2,500 meters in one hour. All eleven safely reached the finish line, showing remarkable spirit. The entire team continued to play in the riverside bathing area in the afternoon before returning in the evening, it was said.

Ministry of Education Vigorously Implements Compulsory Education 148

Personnel will be sent to various provinces and cities next month to supervise implementation

In order to actively promote compulsory education in all provinces and cities across the country, the Ministry of Education previously issued a circular by Minister Wang and instructed various provinces and cities to actively plan for implementation. The central government approved an appropriation of 240,000 yuan in the 24th year to subsidize the implementation of compulsory education in various provinces and cities. In addition, letters were sent to the Sino-British, Sino-French, Sino-Belgian, and Sino-American Boxer Indemnity Funds to request a subsidy of 800,000 yuan. At the same time, provinces and cities (including counties, local cities, and municipalities directly under the central government) were instructed to raise their own funds. Currently, with the exception of the Boxer Indemnity Fund subsidy, for which no definite allocation has been determined, the central government's subsidy of 2.4 million has been distributed to the provinces. The amount of self-raised funds has been generally determined. Most provinces and cities have had their self-raised compulsory education funding approved by the Ministry of Education, while a few are still under review. In order to further supervise and ensure the effective implementation of compulsory education in various provinces and cities in the 24th year, the Ministry of Education will send a large number of personnel to inspect various provinces and cities in September (after schools have started), and to supervise and guide the educational administrative authorities in the effective promotion of compulsory education. Even remote provinces are said to have personnel dispatched to them.

Siamese Government Alleviates Chinese Public Sentiment by Replacing Minister of Education 150

Temporarily Approves Registration of Chinese Schools and Handles Compulsory Classes. Na's Views on Concluding a Sino-Siamese Commercial Treaty

The Shanghai Chinese Overseas Association received a telegram from overseas Chinese in Siam yesterday, stating that the Siamese government, in order to alleviate the Chinese rice ban movement, has dismissed Bai Shansebapan, the Minister of Education who most severely harmed overseas Chinese education, and transferred him to another position. Navy Captain Jian Xinxinchu Songkanchai was appointed as his successor. After the first group of Siamese inspection delegation returned to Siam, the delegation leader Na expressed his views on concluding a Sino-Siamese commercial treaty. The reporter of the Industry and Commerce News inquired about the situation, as follows:

Minister of Education Transferred to Another Position

Bai Shansebapan, the Siamese Minister of Education, was transferred to the position of Minister of Agriculture on August 1st. The vacant position of Minister of Education was filled by Navy Captain Luan Xinxinchu Songkanchai. According to those familiar with the situation in Siam, this change in the Minister of Education is considered to be closely related to Sino-Siamese issues. The former minister, Bai, was the most active in suppressing overseas Chinese education. In recent years, he unreasonably closed over a hundred Chinese schools, so overseas Chinese had no goodwill towards him. In order to alleviate the Chinese rice ban movement, in addition to temporarily approving the registration of Chinese schools and handling compulsory classes, Bai had to leave his post.

Na's Remarks After Returning to Siam

Two months ago, the reporter from the Chinese-language newspaper "Minguo Daily" visited the Chinese delegation. During the delegation's arrival in port, they had a brief conversation with delegation leader Na. Na first mentioned the warm welcome received from the Chinese government in Nanjing, then stated that Chinese civil groups and the press held quite radical views towards the Siamese government, making the atmosphere quite tense. Finally, Na expressed his opinion, believing that "the closure of schools is to maintain the dignity of the law, and the prohibition of Chinese newspaper personnel is also a matter of law enforcement." Regarding the conclusion of a Sino-Siamese commercial treaty, Na said that it should be handled in its entirety in order to have concrete measures. Regarding the so-called concrete measures, Na said, "Such as the determination of obligations and rights related to nationality, residence, industry, and legal rights. Chinese people have resided in Siam for a long time, and their treatment is no different from that of the Siamese people. After the conclusion of the treaty, the situation will be different." It is worth noting that Na is a second-class people's representative (i.e., appointed by the government) in the Siamese People's Assembly and the secretary of the People's Party Club, holding a considerable position. His remarks are worthy of our attention.

Little Men (20) (1) 161

— Original work by American author Louisa May Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

"Dicky's trouble was having a crooked spine, but he bore his affliction so cheerfully that Jo asked him one day, with her odd bluntness, 'Does being a hunchback give you a good temper? If it does, I'd like one.' Dick was always glad to join in the play with the other children, and to be as happy as they were, for he had a brave spirit in his small body. He had at first been very sensitive about his misfortune, but he had soon forgotten it, and no one dared to mention it to him, for Mr. Bhaer had severely punished a boy who laughed at him.

'God doesn't mind it, for though my back is crooked, my heart is straight,' Dick had said to his tormentor, and Mr. and Mrs. Bhaer had taken the hint, and soon made him believe that they loved him for his heart, and did not care what his body was like, except to pity him, and help him to bear his affliction.

One day, while playing 'Noah's Ark,' some one asked, 'What are you going to be, Dick?'

'Oh, I'm the one-humped camel; can't you see my hump?' was his laughing reply.

'Just so, my good child, that isn't to carry a load, only to go ahead of the others,' said Jo, who was arranging the queer menagerie of lions, tigers, dragons, and snakes.

'I hope others will be kind to the poor afflicted boy, and I think my children have already learned that,' said Mrs. Bhaer, pleased to see the success of her teaching. Dick was hobbling past her at the moment, looking like a very happy, though a very small, camel, beside the strong 'Tommy,' who was strutting along like a very grand elephant."

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 176

— (Ning Yi)

It seems that the world is full of dead people who are not good. The eulogy in the obituary is to say good things for the scapegoat. The inscriptions of celebrities are to praise the dead. It seems that the death of such a person is a major loss to the country. No matter how the deceased was scolded before his death, as long as he is rich, he can always ask for praise from others. He was a local tyrant before his death, but the words "Down with local tyrants" will never be found in the obituary. So I always think that it is always good to die.

A young man who has just entered society is like a rough stone, showing a strong spirit of resistance. After hitting a wall, it is as if the stone corners are gradually being worn away. By the time the stone corners are gone, the ambition has been exhausted.

"For the sake of my father getting old, for the sake of my stomach getting hungry, otherwise I really don't want to come to society to see such unbearable ugliness." These are a few indignant words in a friend's letter, but I think that the various ugliness displayed in society are exactly the philosophy of life that cannot be found in books.

The Posture on Qimei Road 177

— Zhang Muliang

This is a road leading directly from Avenue Joffre to New Shanghai. The noise and clamor throughout the day are enough to reveal its true and weary state.

When the sun has just shot its powerful rays from the clouds, everything on Qimei Road has already begun its lively and noisy performance!

Private cars, company cars, school buses from various universities, and tall, cumbersome freight trucks, one after another... trailing wisps of green smoke behind them, scurrying along the asphalt-paved spine of Qimei Road. And there are also those Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau dung carts, clattering and rumbling. So, the mornings on Qimei Road are only filled with these things spiritedly intertwined.

At the entrance to Qimei Road, there are many "Bent Waist Brand" cigarette stalls, using the packaging of brands like "Beautiful Brand," "Golden Mouse Brand," "Company Brand," etc., but inside they are filled with their own manufactured "Bent Waist Brand" cigarettes, neatly stacked in packs. They often tout their wares to rickshaw pullers, laborers, and other such figures, saying: "Hey! These cigarettes are top-notch, only five coppers a pack..."

This can be said to be a major stronghold for people from Jiangbei. They are used to being "Big Good Guys," and if they encounter timid people, they will drag you to a teahouse to reason with you, and incidentally fleece you!

The shops here are lined up along the front of Qimei Road. Several shops have installed those captivating radios to attract customers, but only a few listeners can be seen in front of their stores.

On both sides of the First Qimei Road Bridge, there are many settlements of impoverished people from Jiangbei. Most of them live in simple thatched huts, but quite a few also use boats as dwellings. The stench from all directions here penetrates people's noses with the wind, and that smell is terribly uncomfortable!

From the Second Qimei Road Bridge onward, a completely rural scene unfolds. The fields are filled with green, red, yellow... these colors dotting Qimei Road, as if it were a beautiful painting. Further on, towards the city center, it's another scene entirely.

When government agencies and other institutions dismiss their offices, their cars are mostly active on Qimei Road, taking office staff back home.

When the sun is close to the horizon, streetlights on Qimei Road light up as if by tacit agreement. The flat Qimei Road lies quietly under the half-lit, half-dark streetlights.

— Juan Yin

Little Western Paradise 179

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seventeen: Do Not Ask a Woman's Body, Hard to Speak of Hidden Pain, Strive to See the Face of a Noble, Together Admire High Moral Character

Some of the more inquisitive travelers asked the porters carrying luggage, "What official business does the commissioner have coming to the Northwest?" The porter casually replied, "Investigating cases." Hearing this, and recalling that his face was as dark as the bottom of a pot, resembling Bao Zheng, everyone guessed that this person must be "clearer than the Yellow River" and worthy of a look for his incorruptibility. So, they all waited eagerly at the road entrance. Everyone thought that in a place like Xi'an, which had suffered from drought and war, its vitality had not yet recovered, there probably weren't any major cases that would require a central official to investigate. However, since a central official had come, one couldn't say there was absolutely nothing. Therefore, besides curiosity, they also really wanted to see what a noble person looked like. Around four o'clock in the afternoon, the sound of car horns echoed in front of the hotel, signaling that Commissioner Lan had arrived. The few welcoming personnel who had arrived earlier rushed to the hotel entrance to greet him. Zhang Jiefu, with sweat pouring down his face, also followed to the main entrance. At this moment, Mr. Zhang's enthusiastic welcome also reached Zhiqian's ears. He felt that this matter was somewhat unusual, and although he disdained joining such a bustling crowd, he couldn't help but follow the murmuring crowd and slowly walked out. When he reached the front of the hotel, it happened that Commissioner Lan was getting out of the car. The people who had come to admire the commissioner mostly imagined that, while not necessarily having the dark face of Lord Bao, he must be a tall and sturdy official with both literary and martial bearing. But when the representatives dispersed and revealed Mr. Lan, he turned out to be an old man in his fifties, with a thin, angular face, prominent cheekbones, and temples already gray under his hat. He wore a copper-colored silk padded robe, which arched his back high, and his steps were less than a foot long, revealing his slowness. (295)

Imperial Incense Drifting Record 180

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Because the colors of roses cannot be exactly the same for millions of flowers; even on the same flower, the petals often vary in shade; if petals of different shades are collected together and crushed into a liquid, it will be difficult to obtain a bright, even-colored rouge; at least it cannot be compared to a fresh rose with a very normal color. Therefore, after picking many roses, we must inspect them one by one, only picking off the petals with normal colors for use, and discarding all the rest; this selection work is not only time-consuming, but also cannot be done by a novice without experience..."

As she said this, I immediately understood why I often saw several eunuchs in a certain side hall, carefully picking rose petals around a large bamboo basket as if searching for treasure, it turned out they were for making rouge!

"After enough normal-colored rose petals have been selected," the Empress Dowager continued to explain with relish, "they are then placed in a clean stone mortar and slowly pounded, until the petals become a thick paste; then they are filtered through a fine gauze filter to completely remove all impurities, resulting in the clearest flower juice, and then begins the most important part of making rouge..."

There have always been several squares of bright red silk cotton on the Empress Dowager's dressing table, which I have long known; at this moment, she picked up one at random and lightly cut off a very small piece with a pair of small gold scissors. (395)

The Front and the Back 181

— Zhou Xian

Feeling particularly bored, I picked up a copy of "Dream of the Red Chamber," and it happened to be the section where Uncle Rui was looking at the Fengyue Mirror. After reading it once, I suddenly felt a sense of enlightenment.

I remember just the day before yesterday, a friend said to me, "If you see a pleasing woman on the street with an alluring figure and rich curves, it's best to follow her closely, admiring her from behind, but you must never go in front of her and look back at her face. Because when you look from behind, you can idealize her beauty. But if you look at her face, nine times out of ten, you will be disappointed. You must know that in all the world, perfect beauties are so rare that you might not find one or two in ten thousand."

At the time, I listened to his profound argument without committing myself. Now, comparing it to the theory of the front and back of the Fengyue Mirror, I couldn't help but suddenly understand my friend's profound argument.

However, after thinking carefully, I feel that my friend's words are incorrect. Look, the Fengyue Mirror shows the enchanting Wang Xifeng when viewed from the front, and an empty, hollow skeleton when viewed from the back. The author's painstaking advice is to persuade people to understand that beauty is a skeleton, and a skeleton is beauty. Now my friend is still advising me to imagine the beauty of a woman's face by looking at her back, wouldn't that be like imagining the beauty of Wang Xifeng while looking at the skeleton on the back of the Fengyue Mirror? Wouldn't that be hastening one's own demise?

Therefore, I think that when you see women with attractive backs on the street, you should treat their backs as the front of the Fengyue Mirror, and rush to the front to look at their faces. Because there are no perfect beauties in the world, and although the face of a woman with a slender figure may not be a skeleton, it may be a ghastly woman. If you can regard this ghastly woman as a skinless, fleshless skeleton, then that would naturally be even more thorough. This is what is called reflecting the Fengyue Mirror from the back.

Pidgin English and Russian English 182

— (Ziqiang)

In the lower classes of Shanghai society, the most prevalent forms of English are two: Pidgin English and Russian English. This is not a universal phenomenon, but it is the case for the lower classes of Shanghai and for Russian émigrés.

In Shanghai, we often hear a kind of Pidgin English in circulation:

He is he, me is me,

Is is yes, is is no.

At the same time, we may also hear Russian émigrés begging for coppers on the street, using a kind of Pidgin English to say to you: "Chinamanisgoodman," meaning that Chinese people are good people. But this kind of English is inevitably shallow and laughable.

Little Common Knowledge

Emergency Treatment for Insect Stings and Snake Bites 183

— Bingyu

Emergency Treatment for Insect Stings: In hot weather, various pests breed very quickly, and our bodies are often harmed by them. Therefore, we should know the methods of emergency treatment for everyday life at home. (1) When stung by bees or gadflies, apply tobacco oil from a dry tobacco pipe to immediately relieve pain, or apply the juice of sweet potatoes or morning glory leaves. (2) When bitten by centipedes or millipedes, crush the leaves of knotweed or soybean leaves and apply the juice to the affected area to relieve pain. If ineffective, rub with plum flesh for remarkable results. (3) When stung by dragonflies, wash with vinegar to disinfect. (4) When stung by slugs, the skin swells; apply sesame oil to reduce swelling and remove toxins. (5) When bitten by bedbugs, apply Opodeldoc containing ammonia, but undiluted ammonia is very strong and causes skin pain. You can ask the pharmacy to prepare the following mixture: (10 grams of ammonia, 10 grams of clear water, 2 grams of menthol, 1 gram of camphor, 70 grams of alcohol). (6) When stung by mosquitoes, crush salt and chrysanthemum leaves to extract juice and apply it; the pain and itching will stop immediately. (7) For stings from other poisonous insects such as hairy caterpillars and gnats, knotweed leaf juice can be used to relieve pain. Generally, doctors mainly use persimmon juice, mint, ammonia water, etc. If the skin is swollen and red, lead sugar water (i.e., aluminum acetate) must be used. It is now summer, and everyone suffers from mosquitoes, but the reactions to mosquito bites vary depending on individual constitutions. Some people's skin immediately becomes red and swollen after being bitten, while others do not. We must not scratch the itch, because if scratched, it can easily fester. You can usually go to the pharmacy to buy the following medicines: one is antipruritic lotion, which consists of 2 grams of carbolic acid, 1 gram of menthol, and 100 grams of alcohol; the second is decongestant ointment, which consists of 15 grams of zinc oxide, 1 gram of carbolic acid, 5 grams of Mucelago Tragacanthae, 2 grams of Glycerinum, and 8 grams of water.

Treatment for Snake Bites: There are many types of venomous snakes, the most dangerous being the viper, but the severity of the injury depends on the climate at the time of the bite and the symptoms of poisoning. If the bite is near the heart, immediately tie the bitten area tightly with a rope to prevent the flow of arterial blood, then cut open the bitten area and use your own mouth to suck out the venomous blood, and apply caustic potash. Also use a 5% solution of potassium permanganate to rub the area near the bite, and then inject 1% Calcaria Chlorala before loosening the tied area. Finally, bandage with cotton soaked in a 0.01% Cresloi Saponatu solution. For local treatment, immediately drink alcohol to stimulate excitement after being bitten, and give camphor injections Camphosa Depurata, Drgitalis, and other heart stimulants, or use diaphoretics, diuretics, or large amounts of glucose solution and Liqucr Pingeni injections to dilute the toxins in the body through circulation. There is also a very simple method: wash the area locally with fresh persimmon juice, because persimmon juice can neutralize snake venom.

Free Talk

Decadence in Modern Literature 184

— Meiyu

In modern English literature, Lawrence's mysticism and Joyce's psychoanalysis can naturally represent the characteristics of English bourgeois literature. Lawrence's works almost all involve issues of sexuality, and he emphasizes psychological analysis; however, what he writes is not conscious, nor subconscious, but unconscious; that is to say, he omits descriptions of normal psychology and only describes those unconscious thoughts that are suppressed deep within the heart (which is greatly related to the emphasis on sexual issues in the subject matter). As for Joyce, in Radick's words, he believes that the artist's task is to take a photograph of a dung heap through a microscope; he admits that the writer should write like a slow-motion film, scene by scene, regardless of whether the action is mental or physical, until it ends. He does not realistically represent real life in his works, but simply throws up some trivial, unrelated things, and patches them together to be finished. His representative work "Ulysses" and J.V. Woolf's "Mrs. Dalloway" both use a book to write about the protagonist's psychology in a single day, walking a step, saying a word, the thoughts of smoking a cigarette are all written in the book. (Here we may as well add that Lawrence, Joyce, Woolf, and T.S. Ehot are collectively known as the four giants of the current English literary scene.) Similarly, the French novelist Proust also has the same tendency; he carefully describes some of the most irrelevant actions, and with his special—French bourgeois and the most special part of the aristocracy—the smallest number of figures in a dominant position with extremely fine descriptions, but in this respect, he touched the unparalleled depth and breadth. Thus, we know that these writers all have this kind of trump card, and in writing, they all play with this kind of mystery; but the method of psychoanalysis, when it was discovered at the beginning of the nineteenth century, was originally used as an extremely clever tool to dissect and understand life, but today it is used by them to cover up and embellish the heroic appearance of living reality.

Naturally, this attitude of theirs in creation has its social basis. When the bourgeoisie retreats from progress to conservatism and gradually declines, when the freedom of art, the stubbornness of creative thought, the possibility of the existence and development of transcendent literature, and the independence of literature from society and politics are all passionately advocated and supported, many writers unconsciously narrow their scope of observation of real life, abandon its broad and comprehensive research, and stop at the "solitude of their own souls," and then, due to a lack of real-life knowledge, the deepening and stubbornness of self-thought, they hide in the fruitless attempt to "know themselves." Thus, individualism is transformed into egocentrism. This is the reason for the decline of bourgeois literature in the twentieth century, and the reason for the production of these declining works, and the reason why we call this type of writer decadent.

Furthermore, we say that these writers are decadent because their works, whether good or bad, can only be produced when a certain culture reaches its declining period. This type of work is not only produced today, but also in the declining periods of various cultural stages in history. We usually call it "Byzantinism," and this term fully reveals this meaning. As for us calling them decadent writers, it is not to say that Joyce, Proust, etc. are not great writers. On the contrary, because this decadence itself has its active aspects; like Joyce, etc., they have reached an unprecedented height in analytical intelligence and sensitivity. This is just as Hegel said: "The owl of Mineva (the goddess of wisdom) flies at night." The afterglow of the setting sun of each culture is sometimes more lovely than anything else about it.

However, are there differences between the works of writers such as Shakespeare, Goethe, and Racine and the works of writers such as Joyce, Proust, and Lawrence? I think this is easy to understand. Naturally, modern bourgeois writers are intelligent, sensitive, and have a wider and richer literary tradition than their predecessors. But among their works, there are peculiar and bizarre things that cannot be found in the works of their predecessors. I think it is undeniable that one cannot say why, and even dare not admit that this feature exists. Undoubtedly, a correct explanation of this phenomenon can only be achieved under the illumination of a new methodology. I think these writers are part of the existing culture, and the existing culture is rapidly falling apart. Only this can explain the characteristics of the works of these great modern writers.

Finally, we must also understand whether we should learn from these writers with decadent tendencies? This is a question that has been debated a lot in our publishing industry, and anyone can affirm it without hesitation. But the key is whether we should listen to their commands, or have our own direction? If our writers can deeply understand what kind of writer Joyce is and have his correct worldview, then Joyce will not only not hinder us, but can also give us many benefits; we must study his works and learn from him how to handle the important subject of content and form. We believe that great writers should not only learn from classical works, but also from decadent bourgeois literature. Only the method developed from the most refined historical heritage is the greatest and most correct creative method.

Tragedy by the Sea (8) 185

— Original by French writer Balzac, translated by Wang Jiansheng

It took the fisherman no more than a minute or two to relate this story, even simpler than my account of my own commission. Ordinary people tell a story without thinking; they only narrate the facts that moved them, shaping them into sentences according to how they felt. Therefore, such narration is as sharp and incisive as a splitting ax.

"I don't want to go to Batuts anymore!" Baoling said as we reached the higher side of the lake. We returned to Nakrolayxick along the salty wetlands. Our fisherman became as silent as we were, leading us through confusing paths. Our souls underwent a great transformation, and we were immersed in melancholy thoughts, caused by seeing Chai Bo and knowing his tragedy. We all knew that our guide was silent because he was thinking about those three people. The misfortune of these three appeared clearly before our eyes, like a performance in a tragedy, and his father's atonement was the climax of this play. We dared not look far at the rock where the unfortunate man sat, a great terror to the villagers. As we witnessed a scene of misery never before seen in our lives, dark clouds covered the sky, and smoke rose from the horizon to the sky. We trudged on the desolate and impure soil and salty wetlands, which could be called a place of ground-born diseases. The ground was divided into many unequal squares, each square surrounded by a gray mud pit and filled with salt water, on which salt had coagulated. Within this artificial depression, there were boundaries, and workers carrying plows moved about on it. They despised the few marsh people, the specific name for salt makers. These people, or rather, these Bredon people, wore special clothes, a white short coat, like a distiller. They only intermarried with their own tribe; in this tribe, there was no example of a woman marrying someone other than a salt maker. The terrible appearance of these marshes, dotted with regular mud squares, and the gray earth, which did not grow any Bredon flowers and plants, harmonized with the bleakness that had once pierced our souls. When we reached the small bay where fresh water flowed in, the barren plants that decorated the beach gave us great joy. As we were passing through, we could see the small island where the Chai Bo Lamei family had once lived standing in the lake; we quickly turned our heads away.

Reaching our inn, we noticed a billiard table placed in a ground-floor room. When we learned that this was the only public billiard table in the Nakrulo Yixi area, we packed our bags overnight, preparing to leave, and the next day, we were already in the city of Julun Di. (The End)

Not a Common Bunch (Continued) 186

— Zhou Wen

The host slightly furrowed his brows, smiling and squinting at Pale Face’s reddening face; Pale Face also furrowed his brow slightly, returning a smile.

“I think the magazine business is more profitable, at least we should see a bit of interest…”

The host squinted at Pale Face again; but this time Pale Face kept his eyes fixed ahead, sitting at the table next to the dressing mirror, sipping the newly served covered bowl of tea. As he picked up the poetry manuscript the host had passed over, Round Face’s voice drilled into his ears again:

“I definitely have to do this magazine business… and I’ll definitely hire an editor with a reputation…”

The host kept watching Pale Face as he stood there blankly with his mouth half-open, his gaze fixed on the title of the poetry manuscript. He frowned, but immediately his ears were drawn to Round Face's voice:

"It doesn't matter if the salary is a bit high, the deeper you plant, the bigger it grows..."

The host turned his face away; Pale Face followed suit, but immediately their eyes met as the host turned back. He quickly looked away, fixing his gaze back on the poetry manuscript, "Why am I so agitated today?" he thought, his cheeks growing even hotter, wishing the host would just leave. He glanced at the poetry manuscript from the corner of his eye, and sure enough, the host stood up and walked to the square coffee table where the two fat faces were sitting. He gathered his fingers, first lifting the lid of Round Face’s teacup to take a look, then called out:

"Hey, bring some hot water!"

Pale Face was even more powerfully drawn in by this voice, his ears perked up, focusing intently on the side facing the host and Round Face, desperately trying to hear every word of the host’s request to “edit” the magazine; but at the same time, he musically hoped: "Oh, please don't say it, once it's said, it's over!" He strained his ears for a long time, but still couldn't hear the host and Round Face talking, and felt a kind of dissatisfaction, but he endured it; but finally, he couldn't resist anymore, and turned his face to look. He breathed a deep sigh of relief—it turned out the host was gone, and only the two fat faces were talking face to face. He tilted his head to look in the dressing mirror beside him, and dozens of bead-like oily droplets were actually protruding from the tip of his pale nose. He took out a small white handkerchief to wipe his nose, then wrapped a little finger in the handkerchief to clean his nostrils. Looking carefully in the mirror again, the tip of his nose was actually shiny and beautiful, like white wax. He turned his face back and saw Round Face looking at him. He put the poetry manuscript on the table and stood up, clasping his hands behind his back, and slowly walked towards the two fat faces. "I want to tell him before the host comes back," he thought. The magazine... But he suddenly stopped in the middle of the room, because from the corner of his eye he saw the host reappear in the doorway. So he immediately bowed, with a leisurely air lowered his face, and brought his newly polished nose close to a wilting purple-red flower in the clump of dried flowers in the vase, wrinkling his nostrils, and said leisurely:

"Mmm, mmm, so fragrant."

The host stood in front of him, bowing apologetically and frowning:

"Oh, I'm so sorry, I'm so busy, I have to ask people to urge the guests, and write articles...! Oh, I'm really neglecting you, really..."

"It's fine, no problem," Pale Face said, raising his face. "This flower is..."

"Heh heh," Round Face suddenly stood up and interjected. "Look at us two, just talking, leaving our distinguished guest out in the cold. Host, if you have something to do, go do it, we can help you entertain the guests. We're all family, right?" As he spoke, his eyes swept over Pale Face and then looked at Tall Fat Face.

"Right, right. Actually, I should help my relative entertain the guests," Tall Fat Face said, also quickly pulling out the chair from behind him, extending a hand with five fat fingers straight, and suddenly shaking his head and reciting: "The flower-lined path—was never—swept—for guests. The humble gate—is only now—opened—for you." Heh heh! Please?"

The host frowned, carefully holding his breath and glancing at Pale Face from the side.

"Okay, go ahead if you have something to do," Pale Face said with a smile, his ears turning red again. "Don't be so constrained by formality, we're all family, it's okay..."

Passing Through Wuchuan 187

— Yuan Chenying

When the car stopped in Wuchuan, "a solitary city amidst ten-thousand-foot mountains," it was already four in the afternoon. The sunlight reflecting off the snow on the eastern mountains was dazzling. The car drove into Wuchuan County, and following the dust-flying car were many people dressed in blue cotton clothes, each with a curious look on their faces, quietly discussing where we came from; some even whispered about our overseas Chinese: "Oh! There are even foreign devils!" After saying this, they seemed afraid of us and quietly slipped away. Replacing them was another large group of people, occasionally with one or two more fashionable women, looking at our girls with admiring eyes.

The car abruptly stopped at the county government gate. We went in to make a phone call to Guihua, asking how the two cars that had left with us were doing. The answer was, "The car broke down, it's already back, it will leave again tomorrow!" Getting this answer, we had no choice but to walk out dejectedly. More and more people were crowding around our car, like at a temple fair: looking at us in what they considered colorful clothes, the women still pointing at our girls.

To wait for those two cars, we had to stay here overnight. However, in this small county town, the houses were scattered and dilapidated, there were no large hotels, where could we find lodging for so many people? With great difficulty, we barely found two places: the girls stayed at a girls' elementary school, the boys found another place, and I was fortunate enough to find a friend who was a schoolteacher in this small town, and stayed at his place for one night.

Separating from our companions, I walked to the place of my friend, as young as I was, who had come to this solitary city for a living: it was a boys' elementary school on a slope, the light of a kerosene lamp flickering in the darkness. Entering the room, I was hit by a nauseating odor. I couldn't say what kind of stench it was, I just felt like throwing up. Seeing my expression, my young friend smiled and said, "This is the smell from the coal in the stove. This kind of coal has been buried underground for a short time, and hasn't completely turned into coal. Burning it produces a very foul smell, but it's very cheap, a thousand pounds can be bought for one dollar. Poor families and public institutions all burn this kind of coal!" I asked him, "Wouldn't burning this kind of coal suffocate people?" He laughed and said, "That's okay! If it did, wouldn't I have died long ago? This coal stinks, but it doesn't suffocate people!" Thinking about how my young friend was struggling for a living, leaving his warm home, becoming a "Waiting-for-One-to-Walk-Behind-the-Mountains" (Note 1), and his ability to endure these hardships, compared to the slightly more comfortable life I lived in Guihua City, I was ashamed and speechless.

When drinking water, I felt that the water was not only salty and difficult to drink, but also had a strange odor. But thinking about what had just happened, I didn't say anything. Seeing me frown when drinking water, my friend said, "This water is very salty and hard to drink, right? I'm afraid it's even harder to drink if you add some! This water is well water, it's what ordinary people drink. There's another kind of spring water several miles outside the city, which is as good to drink as the Imperial Spring Well water in Guihua City (Note 2), but only the rich can afford to buy and drink it..." He seemed very emotional as he said this, and I was amazed by his attitude.

After eating dinner at my friend's place, although very tired, I still wanted to go out and take a look, so I followed my friend to the girls' school to see our traveling girls.

The girls were singing hand in hand in the courtyard in twos and threes. Looking in the darkness, listening to the melodious singing, I couldn't help but think that this seemed like another world, it didn't seem like traveling in the desolate borderlands!

At the girls' school, I talked to the middle-aged headmaster for a few words: there are more than four thousand people in this city, but only twenty or thirty girls go to school. People in the city and countryside are still afraid that their daughters will be seduced and eloped with if they go to school. Only a few graduate and go to Guihua for further studies.

When walking back to my friend's place to sleep, the night had fallen deeply, the people who had been watching us had all gone home, leaving only the silent streets, and the barking of dogs was heard from time to time. Listening to my friend tell me the story of how the "Wild Ghosts Scrape" (Note 3) had broken into the city the year before, I thought of a woman I knew who had been ravaged by the Wild Ghosts in that turmoil, imagining so many greenwood heroes carrying guns and riding horses at this time... I couldn't help but feel afraid, crawled into the quilt, and quickly fell asleep.

The next day, I followed my friend to a small restaurant to "go for tea." We passed through the main street and went into a small alley, entering a restaurant like a mountain cave. The stench of coal made me dizzy. The room had no plastered ceiling, and soil would fall into our bowls from time to time. The bed and the ground were full of hardworking people, and some small merchants were killing their morning time here.

After eating a few "Shao Mai" (Note 4), we went out to watch our companions ride horses and watch the soldiers stationed here do push-ups... From morning on, many people gathered around to watch us, until eleven o'clock in the morning, when the two cars from Guihua finally arrived.

Note 1: "Waiting-for-One-to-Walk-Behind-the-Mountains" means those who make a living behind Daqing Mountain and have higher occupations.

Note 2: "Imperial Spring Well" is in front of the Dazhao Temple in Guihua. It is said that Emperor Kangxi of the Qing Dynasty once watered his horses here, and it is the sweetest spring water in Suiyuan.

Note 3: "Wild Ghosts Scrape" is what the people of Suiyuan call bandits. Sometimes, the bandits also call themselves "Wild Ghosts Scrape."

Note 4: "Shao Mai" is a special food of the people of Suiyuan, similar to dumplings but with extremely thin skin and smaller than buns. It is the only food for the people of Suiyuan to go to restaurants in the morning.
