Page 19

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

From Japan's Cultural Undertakings to China's Cultural Construction 188

— Xing An

Japan's cultural undertakings have recently become quite developed. They are not only concerned about the construction of cultural institutions at home, but also pay attention to the external promotion of Japanese culture. It is said that this year, the International Culture Section established by Japan with the International Cultural Undertaking Fund has been very effective since its implementation. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has included more than 1.85 million yuan in next year's budget as the International Cultural Undertaking Fund. The allocation of this fund is used to set up the International Cultural Bureau, Japanese Culture Lectures, Japanese Language Teaching Institutes, and Japanese Research Institutes. Some are used for exchange dispatch fees for domestic and foreign scholars and students, Japanese art introduction fees, international competition fees, international cultural promotion fees, and various international cultural group fees. This shows the importance Japan attaches to cultural undertakings. In particular, they are very enthusiastic about promoting Japanese culture abroad.

The strength of a country can be judged by the level of its culture. The reason why several Western countries are dominating the world today is that their culture is more developed than others. After the Meiji Restoration, Japan also became more prosperous day by day with the progress of its national culture. Although they are currently devoted to strengthening their military preparations, they are still tirelessly creating and carrying out various cultural undertakings. They understand that cultural undertakings are of great importance to the development of the country.

Our country is an ancient civilized country in the world, and our culture once shone brightly in history. But this belongs to the past. Compared with Western civilized countries, China's current culture is at least one or two centuries behind. We say this not to increase the ambition of others and destroy our own prestige. Because the facts are as they are, we cannot hide them. Unless we bring out some spiritual civilization to boast about, we have almost nothing in terms of material culture. One flood kills millions of people, which is a natural disaster, but the lack of material construction can be imagined. As for the spiritual civilization that we often boast about, what is it? Even if it is true, I am afraid it is no longer suitable for the lives of modern Chinese people.

Considering the reasons for the decline of our country's culture today, the main one is that Chinese people have never been willing to accept Western material civilization. People often hold a prejudice that material civilization is base, and only spiritual civilization is worth worshiping. However, the so-called culture should include both material and spiritual, and the two are indispensable. Therefore, in the future, if we want the development of Chinese culture, it is very urgent and necessary to fully import Western material civilization.

Recently, the voice of cultural construction in our country has been singing loudly for a while. Looking at the opinions of all parties, some advocate complete Westernization, some advocate Chinese body and Western use, and some advocate taking China as the base. In our view, no matter which direction China's cultural construction takes in the future, accepting Western material civilization should be the most important task that must be done. If we abandon this and do not do it, Chinese culture will still lag behind others even if we work hard for another five hundred years. As for how to use what method to accept Western material civilization? There is only one method mentioned by Mr. Sun Yat-sen, which is to catch up head-on.

The above is about the cultural construction of our country. If we promote our inherent culture abroad, Chinese culture also has its own characteristics that are worth mentioning to introduce to people, so that foreigners can recognize the true face of China. Although we cannot carry out this work as actively as Japan, we must also pay considerable attention to it. Otherwise, the Chinese people imagined by foreigners may always be an uncivilized nation with braids and small feet.

Scattered Notes from Taicheng 189

— Ai Tu

Taishan City, constructed layer upon layer with the blood and sweat of overseas Chinese, is a gorgeous little market. Here are magnificent buildings, huge department stores, brilliant banks, beautiful schools, and the fragrance of luxurious cosmetics. Everything is the capitalist scene of a newly emerging small city.

Many years ago, when overseas Chinese had not yet developed, this was indeed an old market. Later, as overseas Chinese developed more and more in foreign countries, Guangdong, where overseas Chinese remittances were the most abundant, and especially the people of Taishan, developed the most. Therefore, the people here can truly be said to have traveled all over the world. Indeed, the capital power of the overseas Chinese here can be said to occupy an important position in the major cities of the country. For example, taking the situation in Shanghai, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou, the businessmen of Taishan always occupy the first high chair. Therefore, when we go there, we can always see many, many deeds composed of overseas Chinese capital.

The railway here comes from Jiangmen Gongyi in the north to here, and then from here to Guanghai in the south. The highways extending in all directions are like a net. There is also a very convenient small river that can transport many goods from overseas to this great consumer market. All day long, we can hear the continuous rumble of trains or the noisy sounds of whistles in the small city. The gorgeous cars fly back and forth on the flat and neat cement roads. In fact, the roads in the entire Taicheng are the best in the entire county of Guangdong. The two rows of neat foreign-style houses and shops are no different from the prosperous streets of big cities. When standing under the seven- or eight-story buildings, you may wonder if this is a corner of a metropolis.

Every time it's a market day, it becomes particularly noisy here. The people who come into the city from the four villages are mostly simple women. However, if they are young, they are always dressed in a moving way, wandering the streets with the fragrance of cosmetics. In a quiet corner of the city, there are mostly places for young men and women to enter and exit. In Taicheng, we can see many, many girls dressed like flower branches and handsome men in Western clothes together. All of this has become a special and prosperous phenomenon in Taicheng. The strong atmosphere of luxurious capitalism, at least, is something I cannot deny. Even the tall and beautiful buildings are enough to match the fact that this is a very famous market in the south, and it is a consumer market. However, until recently, after groups of unemployed overseas Chinese returned, overseas Chinese stopped remitting money. As a result, everything here inevitably suffered the impact, and a scene of decline and calm gradually arose. Everything was masked with sadness. And on the streets, "Great Discount" signs are hanging everywhere, fluttering in the wind. No different from big cities, the general feeling of the people is also "indifferent and cold."

When walking slowly from the train station to the streets of Taicheng, we can still see some lively children jumping and walking around. This is a good result of the development of education in Taishan. However, in recent years, due to the unemployment of overseas Chinese and the cessation of remittances, education has also been significantly affected and bankrupt. The number of students in the fourteen or five secondary schools has also been greatly reduced. At the same time, young people who have returned from studying abroad or have graduated from universities in China are scattered in the countryside like sand. As a result, there is a fierce competition for the teaching positions where "there are more monks than porridge," making a mess.

Turning a bend from the southeast corner of the city, the most famous middle school is outside. That gorgeous school building was built with more than 600,000 yuan of overseas Chinese blood and sweat. Therefore, such a school building is quite remarkable. However, I heard that the academic performance inside is very bad, which is also an inevitable phenomenon in Chinese society.

Taking the train from here to the south, you can reach the coast of the South China Sea, and then drift out to the South Pacific Ocean across this sea.

The Sun's Words 190

— Ji Tuan

When I was a child, when the smile of childhood had not yet disappeared from my face, I remember how much I loved this supple, snake-like night! Yes, the boundless, silent voice of the night, like a calm sea without wind or waves; the moon's light, like mountain spring water, brought endless, unspoken comfort and remembrance from afar, from the other side of the rivers and mountains; and also! Ah, that forever young (perhaps never aging) light and laughter, the strong flavor of life's enjoyment, the strong flavor of tobacco and wine, these seemed to be marked on the black board of the night with large words and exclamation points: "The night, with its licentiousness, decay, and enjoyment, belongs to young people, forever belongs to young people!"

(Damn it! Does that mean that in these difficult and declining years, young people are only allowed to have this string of numbness and intoxication? Is this "beneficial" for some people? Is it possible that...?)

The night! With its strange quirks and posture, with its cyan and red coat and smile, existed in my shallow childhood days, when life had not yet become a problem of trouble, when the bright smile still remained on the young face...

But year after year, struggling in a not-so-easy life, learning to get by, the dreams and laughter of childhood disappeared, and the mind was occupied by another mysterious problem day and night. The childlike heart was aging day by day, making me forget all the gilded days of false qualities.

(The night is still lingering in my heart, so long, so deep, with no news of awakening! Perhaps she no longer has a charming appearance, but is like life, taking on a gloomy face, with an ever-darkening heart.)

In that way, I forgot about morbid, dim enjoyment; but for the daytime, because it housed many ugly aspects of life that were completely different from ideals, deception, foolishness, and the old troubles of all people; and, what was most unbearable, there was a big, dazzling sun shining there!

The light was so bright that it stung people's vision, making them dare not open their eyes to face it directly, the heat was so scorching that it burned people's skin and could daze their brains. It was the sun that revealed the rusty copper truth of the gilded life at night, which was enough to make people unhappy, enough

Page 20

to make people afraid and disgusted.

But finally, on an unexpected day, I saw the value of the sun in another kind of light.

One morning—an early morning. The surroundings were still quiet, and the hustle and bustle of the world could not be heard; in the trees, birds were sparsely chirping, the remnant stars were still twinkling, and I, as if I had finished a long journey, suddenly woke up from my dream in a hurry.

Braving the morning air, I quietly walked to the suburbs; it was the weather of early autumn, dew glistening on the grass, the wind was gentle, and dissolved the breath of soil and plants.

The sun—this sun! It had silently hung up. Looking at it, it was easy to think of Turgenev's poem "Morning"; it spread its light wide on the ground, still so dazzling, so hot.

Gradually, getting used to it, I began to find it kind: looking at its face: serious, enthusiastic, truly golden; basking in it, like immersing myself in the hot spring water of Egypt, warm and firm, where darkness and indifference did not exist!

So, I began to learn to use it, letting it drape over my whole body, unafraid, and without rushing, I tried a sunbath, the doctor had advised me: "In treatment, sunlight is a priceless medicine."

So I thought: In the daily life of getting closer to the sunlight, my body may become a little better, my skin may no longer be so pale and loose, and all the health deficiencies may gradually disappear, right?

A feeling of spiritual comfort made me unable to speak my gratitude, I only felt: being able to have the sun permanently is the greatest happiness in the world.

From this moment on, I began to feel the value of the sun, and recognized the gloom and pretense of the night.

Mr. Shen 191

— Shi Ying

Long years and a difficult life have refined Mr. Shen's character to be like that of a child. In his sixties, he spends every day with children around the age of ten. Tears, snot, rulers, dog-eared books, and the clamor of recitations. Mr. Shen looks at this group of twenty or thirty kowtowing children, like a cluster of buzzing golden flies on rotten meat, while he himself observes serenely, with a satisfied smile.

A child recites Tang poetry in a drawn-out tone: "Left home young, return old, / Accent unchanged, but hair grown gray. / Children see me, do not know me, / Smiling, they ask, 'Where do you come from, guest?'" Mr. Shen loves this poem the most. He listens to it with longing, lightly tapping the table as if keeping time. Whenever he hears this poem, he cannot help but quietly recall his childhood in his old and lonely heart—the autumn sun in the courtyard, painting the slender, pale shadows of sunflowers, gently trembling on the white wall, and soft white clouds leisurely drifting across a corner of the blue sky. It is as if it were still late spring. … His youth was spent entirely in books and examination baskets. The title of a "Xiucai" (successful candidate in the imperial examination) was the price he paid for ten years of studying by the cold window. He was born into a family of scholars for generations. In this small town, there were few who studied. His father was a "Juren" (successful provincial candidate) and a gentry director, and the income from the fields was enough to keep the family well-fed. In those days, Mr. Shen lived in a carefree era. Although he studied nothing but eight-legged essays and test poems, he was also intoxicated by the situation where "beauty like jade is found in books." On a fine afternoon in spring or autumn, he would take a volume of poetry to the Wanghai Teahouse along the river, brew a pot of tea, and savor the sentences in the book while admiring the sails on the river. He didn't have to do anything. Mr. Shen's future was his father's present. Passing the Juren exam meant becoming a local gentry director, with no worries about food and clothing. Why bother with diligent livelihood? In his eyes, the dream was perfect. But the tide of the times swept away his last hope. The death of his father added to his sorrow, but what saddened him most was that he had to open his eyes and see how the burden of life was added to his weak shoulders. At that time, he was over thirty years old and the father of three children.

Recommended by relatives, he became an accountant in a shop. Abacuses, silver coins, and ledgers—things he usually didn't pay attention to—now became his close companions. Middle-aged emotions, coupled with a cumbersome family, meant that life would no longer rise to any waves. However, the store life, which had never been experienced before, made his temperament dull, and like a lame ox pulling a heavy plow, he hobbled through twenty years. —Twenty years, again this long period of time! People grew old, and the children in the family grew up. His own mouth was covered with a graying beard, but it could not cover his melancholy smile. But before his melancholy smile had faded from the corners of his mouth, the shop where he worked as an accountant closed its doors, and he lost his job. Naturally, for three whole years, he could not find another place. —In his old heart, he thought that he could enjoy his old age at home, but his grown-up sons did not earn enough to be independent. He had no choice but to relive his old dream, opening a private school, recruiting twenty or thirty thin children. On the one hand, he could get some pocket money, and on the other hand, he could pass the boring years. While the children were chanting in long tones, he habitually took out a paper cigarette, watched the curling white smoke, and reminisced about the traceless past. He didn't know if it was regret or remembrance. …

After letting the children of the private school go, Mr. Shen also dragged his aging steps to go outside for a walk. But he was no longer in the mood to go to the Wanghai Teahouse. This old shop, which had been through thirty or forty years of weathering, was still as it always had been.

Seaside 192

— Cun Yin

(Blue sea, red sea, laughing sea, roaring sea.)

In the morning? Strolling along the coast, a kind of vast, solid feeling, like rice, fills my stomach; it simply fills me up, and that boundless freshness is endlessly, endlessly there.

The morning sun is as beautiful as a young girl. If my hand could touch its tenderness, then I would say, "It is as gentle as velvet!" And the rolling sea is even more beautiful than the sun, than velvet. Sometimes it dances, and sometimes it hums a Picnic-style tune that is both sorrowful and light.

(I like listening to the occasional roar that flies by and stimulates my nerves.)

But at noon, the sun's face is stretched taut like iron.

(I do not hear any delicate music of nature, I do not see any moving dances of nature. I am frightened, I only know that the sea is fast asleep.)

The gentle sea sleeping under this violent sun is as pitiful as a cow about to be slaughtered. But who can ask this violent sun to become more gentle?

That seaside, how pitiful! It seems to be telling me:

"These days are really hard to bear!"

For the suffering of the sea, I also suffer. I have to close my eyes and quietly try to fall asleep quickly. Listening to the hot sea breeze lazily crawling, crawling over my body, it seems that a million weights of pain all belong to me.

(Blue sea, red sea, laughing sea, roaring sea.)

In the evening, the fishermen row back from afar. They drink the blood of the sea and catch the cells of the sea.

(Watching the seaside at dawn and dusk is that towering pale peak. Counting one, two, three, four... walking from here to there, it should make you forget the number of your steps. But standing on the seaside and looking back, in a few seconds, you can immediately see that pale peak. It is passionately comforting the seaside, it is like a young boy who has just come of age, flirting with this beautiful girl. And when the emotions between them become so intense that they cannot be more intense, the peak will emit smoke, and the peak will give its own small soul to this tender girl—and then, the people who live there will suffer panic. When they are in turmoil, the soul of the peak and the seaside kiss each other sweetly. They embrace.

The moon comes out. The seaside's tenderness instantly forgets the pain of noon.

Men and women, as lively as a cherry blossom festival, some dragging canvas chairs, setting up small round tables, with their beer.

However, the fishermen over there, carrying bright lights and chewing on the leftovers from their evening meal, are about to step onto their fishy fishing boats to work again.

Those who swim in the sea and drink beer on the seaside do not pay attention to the hard work of these tiny fishermen; they are indifferent to suffering that is not their own!

Yes, the seaside is extremely beautiful, harmonized by the moonlight. But the girl-like sea wakes up, and it roars. ——

Movie News

Depiction of New Era Figures 198

— (Tomorrow)

(1) Everyone knows that Ye Qianyu is a nationally renowned cartoonist, but they don't know that he has long been in the film industry. He drew Mr. Wang on paper, and now he has put him on the screen. We think that the creator of the hilarious Mr. Wang, who makes people want to laugh at first sight, must be a humorous person with Mr. Wang's demeanor. If you think that way, then you are completely wrong. His appearance is short and agile, his personality is sincere and harmonious, and he has the full demeanor of an artist. But he is now the manager of the New Era Company. You must think that artists cannot handle affairs, right? In fact, this is another mistake. He can not only handle all affairs, but he handles them very well. You see the New Era Company developing day by day, which is the result of his work.

(2) The name Tang Jie should not be unfamiliar, but he is now surnamed Wang instead of Tang. Only Ye Qianyu probably knows why he is surnamed Wang. If readers want to ask me what Tang Jie looks like, then I would like to ask you to look at Ye Qianyu's Mr. Wang cartoon. If it is still not clear enough, then you should go and see Mr. Wang on the screen. You can clearly see Tang Jie's true face on the screen, and you can also discover the reason why he is surnamed Wang. He has changed a bit since he came back from Suzhou. Miss Hu Die was the first to see him and asked in surprise, "Mr. Wang, why are you so dark and thin?" Tang Jie couldn't help but sigh and said, "I recently went to the countryside, and the countryside is bankrupt. The farmers are trapped in deep water and fire. My being so dark and thin is just one ten-thousandth of the people's suffering that I brought back from the countryside. The whole picture of the bankrupt, pitiful, and ridiculous countryside, you can see it again when I finish filming the interior scenes." After hearing this, Miss Hu couldn't help but feel sad for a long time.

(3) We only know Cao Xuesong as a writer, but we don't know when he actually became a clown. According to him, he has his philosophy of being a clown. Naturally, in this day and age, it is rare and valuable to laugh yourself and make others laugh as well. His nickname is Little Chen, but Little Chen is not small. If you have seen the Mr. Wang movie, you will know what he looks like. He returned from Suzhou this time without filming. He said to people, "Although I didn't act in front of the camera when I went to Suzhou, I did a very wonderful job in the play of life." After speaking, he gave a smug smile. There are many mysteries hidden in this smile.

(4) The name Jiang Ming was very familiar to people four or five years ago, but since then there has been a long period of separation. It is said that he unfortunately had lung disease and slept in the hospital for three years. Now he has recovered his health, and we very much hope to see his elegance on the stage again, but he has also changed his career recently. He is a screenwriter in the New Era Company. The Mr. Wang film has been widely welcomed. Although no audience will pay attention to this unnamed hero behind the scenes, he is particularly interested in this behind-the-scenes work. He said that he was a loyal audience of the drama of life on this trip to Suzhou. Therefore, Cao Xuesong's mystery did not dare to be displayed in front of him. He could see everything clearly, the moonlight of the Caiyun Bridge, the carriages in the tree-lined avenue... According to him, he will write a story about "Suzhou's Carriages." I don't know what is carried on these carriages. Let's wait and see. (To be continued)

Shen Bao Local Supplement Car Weekly

New Trends in the US Automotive Industry Over the Past Half Year 203

— (Shadowy Fool)

Mid-Priced Cars Suddenly Show Activity

If we observe the history of the American automotive industry, the production and sales figures undoubtedly reached their peak in 1929. Starting in 1930, a wave of recession began to stir, and the entire United States was filled with a bleak atmosphere. Nineteen out of every ten industrial and commercial sectors were affected, and the automotive industry was naturally no exception, suffering considerable impact.

Therefore, after the onset of the recession, the number of cars produced by various American automakers suddenly declined. Recalling the heyday of the automotive industry in 1929, American automakers produced a total of 5,622,000 vehicles that year. Subsequently, this number decreased to 3,510,000 vehicles in 1930, 2,472,000 vehicles in 1931, 1,431,000 vehicles in 1932, 1,986,000 vehicles in 1933, and 2,896,000 vehicles in 1934. From the figures, we can see that the production of American cars decreased year by year starting from 1930, with the lowest production in 1932, only a quarter of that in 1929. Production increased again from 1933, but it was still far from the levels of 1929.

Because the production in 1933 increased compared to 1932, and 1934 was even higher than 1933, the leaders of the American automotive industry became optimistic, believing that the era of recovery for the American automotive industry had arrived. Therefore, at the end of 1934, all car manufacturers increased production in their 1935 business plans, believing that the total American car production in 1935 would be at least four million. Since the beginning of 1935, the sales of new cars have indeed shown sudden activity, with production and sales figures exceeding one million vehicles in the first quarter. Although the exact statistics for the first half of the year have not been officially released, it can be asserted that they are above two million vehicles. Therefore, the goal of producing four million cars for the entire year is likely achievable, and it is no wonder that American automakers are excited.

If we classify the cars produced by American manufacturers based on their selling prices, we can divide them into three categories: high-priced, mid-priced, and low-priced. In the past, low-priced cars had the highest sales, followed by mid-priced cars, and high-priced cars had the lowest sales. This was naturally an immutable rule. However, after 1929, even in terms of percentages, the sales of low-priced cars increased year by year, while the sales of mid-priced and high-priced cars decreased year by year. The only reason for this was that, under the raging tide of the recession, the economic strength of the average American citizen was weakened, and they were unable to purchase mid-priced or higher cars. At the same time, advancements in automobile manufacturing engineering made low-priced cars as stable, fast, and safe as high-priced cars. So, if one were to buy a high-priced car, why not buy a low-priced car that offers more value for money? Based on the two reasons mentioned above, the sales of low-priced cars almost completely captured the market share of mid-priced and high-priced cars.

However, things took an unexpected turn. Since the beginning of this year, the sales of mid-priced cars have suddenly increased in terms of percentages. As a result, people in the automotive industry have become even more confident in the recovery of the car industry due to the activity of mid-priced cars. All automotive industry leaders have said that, under these circumstances, a general recovery of the automotive industry is possible. Recalling the increases in automobile production by American manufacturers in 1933 and 1934, these were all due to improved sales of low-priced cars. In terms of percentages, low-priced cars increased year by year, while mid-priced and higher cars decreased year by year. Therefore, in those years, all car manufacturers still focused their attention on low-priced cars. However, the results showed that, in terms of percentages, the sales of mid-priced cars priced from $650 to $850 increased the most.

In the first four months of this year, the total number of General Motors' Pontiac and Oldsmobile, and Chrysler's Dodge registered throughout the United States reached 148,315 vehicles, an increase of 110.7% compared to the same period last year, while passenger car sales only increased by 60.8%. In May and June, the sales of mid-priced cars continued to increase, just as they did in the first four months. According to a report from Chrysler on June 15, Dodge sales in the last week totaled 4,265 vehicles, an increase of 5.4% compared to the previous week. In the 24 weeks of this year, up to June 15, a total of 90,406 vehicles were sold, an increase of 97.4% compared to the same period last year.

In the first four months, the total number of low-priced cars registered in the United States was 652,353 vehicles, accounting for 73.4% of the total car sales. In terms of quantity, this was an increase of 57% compared to the same period last year, but in the first four months of last year, the percentage of low-priced cars was 75.2%. Therefore, people in the automotive industry have said that the surge in sales of mid-priced cars has proven that society has more money to buy cars. People who were qualified to buy high-priced cars but bought low-priced cars after the start of the recession are now returning to their original state and want to buy more expensive cars.

Automotive News from Abroad 204

— Yu

Statistics on Vehicle Accidents in the UK: In the first six months of 1935, there were a total of 15,000 road vehicle accidents in Great Britain. According to an analysis by the Department of Transport, pedestrians on the road were the most affected, while drivers were the least affected. If we calculate using percentages, pedestrians account for 55.9%, cyclists 20.2%, motorcyclists 12.9%, passengers 6.2%, and drivers 4.8%. Further statistical analysis shows that 85.1% of pedestrians died due to their own carelessness, of which 30.2% were children under the age of fifteen. From these two points of view, it is a fair opinion that the majority of drivers and passengers are very careful while driving. Young children are the most careless about the traffic on the road, and their knowledge of traffic is the most superficial. Therefore, parents and school authorities should pay attention to this matter. On the other hand, driver error accounts for a large percentage of accidents, estimated at 25.1%, with excessive speed being the biggest primary cause of accidents. What is most peculiar is that the time when accidents occur most frequently each day is between 5 pm and 7 pm. It is speculated that the reason for this is that adults are eager to go home from work to rest at this time, so the speed of vehicles increases, and accidents are likely to occur as a result. As for the morning, everyone seems lazy and unwilling to go to the office, so the speed of vehicles is moderate and safer.

Abolition of the US Federal Gasoline Tax: The taxation of gasoline in the United States almost goes through two levels. In addition to state taxes, there are also federal taxes. Because the burden on drivers is too heavy, they have recently requested the abolition of the federal tax. There are 300 organizations participating in this tax abolition movement, representing 21 states. According to statistics, if this tax is removed, it would save taxpayers at least $170,000,000 per year. This is in addition to the $500,000,000 in state taxes and the $350,000,000 in registration fees. For New York State alone, it would cost an additional $13,800,000 per year.

One in One Hundred People Will Be Injured: Because the automotive industry in the United States is very developed, the annual car accident rate is also the highest. According to statistics published in the recent issue of "Public Safety" magazine, one in every hundred people in the United States was injured in a car accident last year. This statistic is based on the number of accidents last year. Last year, a total of 1,250,000 people were injured in car accidents in the United States, and the population of the United States is approximately 125,000,000 people, which is a ratio of one to one hundred. "Public Safety" magazine also based this ratio to tell the public that, "According to the above calculations, if there are two people alive now, one of them is bound to be injured in the next fifty years. One in four people has the possibility of being injured in twenty-five years. One in five people is in danger of being injured in the next twenty years. If a person has twenty close relatives and friends, unless everyone is very careful on the road, one of these twenty people is destined to be injured or even lose their lives in a car accident in the next five years.

The Japanese Automotive Industry 205

— Qin Xiaocun

In 1934, the total value of imported foreign finished automobiles, chassis, tires, etc. to Japan was 41,193,324 Japanese yen. Compared to the import of 22,275,937 Japanese yen in 1930, it has more than doubled.

The annual increase in this import amount has been the case since 1925. After the increase in tariff barriers in 1932, although the quantity of industry imports has been greatly affected, due to the drop in the exchange rate, Japan's automobile imports have not decreased in terms of value.

Due to the progress of the arms industry, the automotive industry in 1934 experienced a surprising increase in both quantity and value. The following table shows its general outline.

Although imports of foreign-made automobiles have surged, domestic automobile manufacturing has also been very active, showing remarkable progress. Nissan Motor Co., Ltd. is considered the leader in the industry. In 1931, the company only manufactured 434 automobiles in one year. After that, it made annual progress. In 1932, it produced 840 vehicles. In 1933, it produced 1,790 vehicles. By last year, 1934, it had increased to 2,500 vehicles. It is expected that the statistics by the end of the year will be more than double this number. In October last year, the export procedures for a large batch of small "Datsun" passenger cars imported from Japan to Australia were managed entirely by Mitsubishi Corporation.

It is said that Nissan Industrial Co., Ltd., which manufactures the aforementioned "Datsun" automobiles, has become one of Japan's well-known large industries and has decided to increase its capital to 200,000,000 Japanese yen, with 99,415,000 yen actually paid up.

Nissan Motor Co., Ltd. has also joined forces with other industry players such as Japan Automobile Co., Ltd. to form a company to raise a large amount of capital specifically for industry lending, pawn lending, and production projects.

The above picture shows the Shunfeng brand all-steel automobile encountering its first accident on the Shanghai-Nanjing Highway. The car was provided by a certain gentleman and was driven by a chauffeur. At that time, due to excessive speed, he lost control, causing the car to suddenly drive to the side of the road. After rolling twice, it plunged from one side of a ditch that was seven feet deep and twenty feet wide, directly to the field on the opposite side of the ditch before stopping. At that time, the front of the car was facing the road, and the body of the car did not overturn. The people in the car, including a young woman holding a child, were all shaken up, but none of them were injured. Even the glass on the car was not shattered. Afterwards, everyone felt deeply fortunate and believed that their survival was due to the Shunfeng brand all-steel automobile.
